Timing and Place of Slaughtering the Hadi
Commentary clarifying temporal and spatial specifications for Hadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the temporal and spatial requirements for the Hadi in the Hanafi school and explain the intra-madhhab differences regarding the timing of slaughter and the vowed badanah.

Core Idea
Hadi timing is wajib only for Tamattu' and Qiran; all Hadi must be in the Haram, but a distinct vowed badanah is an exception.

The Hadi — a sacrificial animal brought to the Haram — is a key component of Hajj. But when and where must it be slaughtered? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, clarifying that while the place is always the Haram, the time is only restricted for Tamattu' and Qiran pilgrims. It also reveals a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement on what happens if the slaughter is delayed, and on the status of a vowed badanah.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two dimensions
The passage separates location (always Haram) from time (only for Tamattu'/Qiran). First, understand that every Hadi — whether obligatory or voluntary — must be slaughtered within the Haram boundary.
The matn states 'wa al-kull bi al-haram'.
2
Identify which Hadi are time-bound
Only the Hadi of Tamattu' (performing 'Umra then Hajj with a break) and Qiran (combining 'Umra and Hajj with one ihram) must be slaughtered on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) or the three Tashreeq days. Voluntary Hadi and others have no fixed time.
Temporal binding is a specification (takhsis) of the general rule.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on timing
According to Abu Hanifa, slaughtering after the Tashreeq days is valid but misses a wajib; before the Day of Nahr is invalid by consensus. The Sahibayn hold that slaughtering any time after entering the state of tahlil (e.g., after shaving) is valid with no penalty, and the sunnah is to slaughter before tahlil.
Abu Hanifa: قبل يوم النحر لا يجزئ بالإجماع; بعد أيام النحر أجزأ إلا أنه تارك للواجب.
4
Analyze the place requirement and the badanah exception
All vowed Hadi must be in the Haram, but a vowed badanah (a specific camel or cow vowed as a symbol of Allah) is not restricted to the Haram according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf analogizes it to vowed Hadi. If the vow specifies 'from the symbols of Allah' or intends Makkah, all agree it is restricted.
The key is the language of the vow – 'badanah' alone does not imply the Haram.
5
Understand the ruling on ta'rif
Ta'rif — publicly marking or taking the Hadi to 'Arafat — is not obligatory. It is recommended for thanksgiving Hadi (shukr) but disliked and recommended to conceal for expiatory Hadi (jinaayah) because of the sin that caused it.
The commentator notes that the matn omitted this detail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وخص ذبح هدى المتعة والقرآن بيوم النحر فقط والكل بالحرم لا بفقيره) بيان لكون الهدي موقتاً بالمكان سواء كان دم شكر أو جناية لما تقدم أنه اسم لما يهدى من النعم إلى الحرم. وأما توقيته بالزمان فمخصوص بهدي المتعة والقران وأما بقية الهدايا فلا تتقيد بزمان. وأفاد أن هدي التطوع إذا بلغ الحرم لا يتقيد بزمان وهو الصحيح، وإن كان ذبحه يوم النحر أفضل كما ذكره الشارح خلافاً للقدوري. وأراد المصنف النحر وقته وهو الأيام بيوم الثلاثة، وأراد بالاختصاص الاختصاص من حيث الوجوب على قول أبي حنيفة وإلا لو ذبح بعد أيام النحر أجزأ إلا أنه تارك للواجب وقبلها لا يجزئ بالإجماع، وعلى قولهما كذلك. القبلية وكونه فيها هو السنة عندهما حتى لو ذبح بعد التحلل بالحلق لا شيء عليه، وعنده في عليه دم. ودخل تحت قوله والكل «بالحرم الهدي المنذور بخلاف البدنة المنذورة فإنها لا تتقيد بالحرم عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف: لا يجوز ذبحها في غير الحرم قياساً على الهدي المنذور والفرق ظاهر واتفقوا على أنه لو نذر نحر جزور أو بقرة فإنه لا يتقيد بالحرم ولو نذر بدنة من شعائر الله أو نوى أن تنحر بمكة تقيد بالحرم اتفاقاً. كذا في المحيط. وقوله «لا بفقيره» بيان لجواز التصدق على فقراء غير الحرم بلحم الهدي لإطلاق الدلائل لكن التصدق على فقراء مكة أفضل كما في البدائع معزياً إلى الأصل قوله: (ولا يجب التعريف بالهدى) لأن الهدي ينبئ عن النقل إلى مكان التقرب بإراقة الدم فيه لا عن التعريف فلا يجب وهو الذهاب به إلى عرفات أو التشهير بالتقليد والإشعار ولم يذكر استحبابه لأن فيه تفصيلاً، فما كان دم شكر استحب تعريفه وما كان دم كفارة استحب إخفاؤه وستره لأن سببها الجناية كقضاء الصلاة يستحب إخفاؤه، ولم يذكر المصنف سنن الذبح والنحر هنا
His saying: (And He specified the slaughtering of the Hadi of Tamattu' and Qiran on the Day of Nahr only, and all in the Haram, not its poor) is an explanation that the Hadi is bound by place, whether it is a blood of thanksgiving or crime, because it was previously mentioned that it is a name for what is offered from camels to the Haram. As for its binding by time, it is specific to the Hadi of Tamattu' and Qiran, and as for the rest of the offerings, they are not bound by time. And he indicated that the voluntary Hadi if it reaches the Haram is not bound by time, and that is correct, although slaughtering it on the Day of Nahr is better as the commentator mentioned, contrary to al-Quduri. And the author meant by 'Nahr' its time, which is the three days; and he meant by 'specification' specification in terms of obligation according to Abu Hanifa, otherwise if he slaughters after the days of Nahr it is valid except that he is leaving the obligatory, and before them it is not valid by consensus, and according to the Sahibayn as well. The beforeness and being in it is the sunnah according to them, so if he slaughtered after tahlil by shaving, there is nothing upon him, while according to him (Abu Hanifa) there is blood upon him. And under his saying 'all in the Haram' enters the vowed Hadi, unlike the vowed camel (badanah) which is not bound by the Haram according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf said: It is not permissible to slaughter it outside the Haram by analogy to the vowed Hadi, and the difference is apparent. And they agreed that if he vowed to slaughter a camel or cow, it is not bound by the Haram, and if he vowed a badanah from the symbols of Allah or intended it to be slaughtered in Mecca, it is bound by the Haram by agreement. Thus in al-Muhit. And his saying 'not its poor' is an explanation of the permissibility of giving charity to the poor of other than the Haram from the meat of the Hadi due to the generality of evidences, but charity to the poor of Mecca is better as in al-Badai' attributed to the original. His saying: (And there is no obligation to define the Hadi) because the Hadi signifies the transfer to the place of seeking nearness by spilling blood in it, not defining, so it is not required, and it is going with it to Arafat or publicizing by making a garland or marking, and he did not mention its recommendation because there is detail in it: what is a blood of thanksgiving, its definition is recommended, and what is a blood of expiation, its concealment and covering is recommended because its cause is crime, like making up a prayer, it is recommended to conceal it. And the author did not mention the sunnas of slaughtering here.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically the statement that 'He specified the slaughter of the Hadi of Tamattu' and Qiran on the Day of Nahr only, and all in the Haram, not its poor.' The commentator explains that the Hadi is generally restricted to the Haram in terms of place for all types, whether they are thanksgiving (shukr) or expiation (jinaayah). However, temporal restriction applies only to the Hadi of Tamattu' and Qiran, which must be slaughtered on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) or the three days after (Tashreeq). Other types, like voluntary Hadi that reaches the Haram, are not time-bound, though slaughter on the Day of Nahr is better. There is a difference within the Hanafi school: according to Abu Hanifa, slaughtering before the Day of Nahr is invalid by consensus; slaughtering after the three days is valid but leaving a wajib. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), slaughtering before tahlil (after shaving) is sunnah, and after tahlil there is no penalty. The passage also discusses the place: the vowed Hadi must be in the Haram, but the vowed badanah (a specific camel) is not restricted to the Haram according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf analogizes it to the vowed Hadi. If one vows a camel or cow without specifying, it is not restricted; if one vows a 'badanah from the symbols of Allah' or intends to slaughter in Makkah, it is restricted by agreement. The phrase 'not its poor' indicates that the meat of the Hadi can be given to poor outside the Haram, though Makkah poor are better. Finally, the text addresses the ruling on 'definition' (ta'rif) of the Hadi: it is not obligatory to publicly mark or take it to Arafat. However, there is a recommendation: for thanksgiving, it is recommended to make it known; for expiation, it is recommended to conceal it, as expiation is connected to sin and should be hidden.

Key Terms
هدي (hadi): An animal brought to the Haram for sacrifice, whether obligatory or voluntary.
بدنة (badanah): A specific camel or cow vowed as a symbol of Allah, sometimes considered separate from general Hadi.
تعريف (ta'rif): Publicly marking or taking the Hadi to Arafat to announce it as a sacrificial animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone slaughters the Hadi of Tamattu' after the days of Tashreeq, what is the ruling?
A) The slaughter is invalid and must be repeated
B) It is valid but he has left a wajib
C) It is valid and no penalty
D) It is invalid but no penalty

Key Takeaway
Only the Hadi of Tamattu' and Qiran is time-bound to the Day of Nahr; all Hadi must be in the Haram, with an exception for a generic vowed badanah.

Timing and Place of the Hady for Tamattu' and Qiran
Commentary on matn rulings about hady timing and place

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the timing and place requirements for slaughtering the hady of tamattu' and qiran, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on slaughtering before and after the days of Nahr.

Core Idea
The hady for tamattu' and qiran must be slaughtered on the day of Nahr in the Haram; before is invalid, after leaves a wajib.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we examine the specific timing and place obligations for the hady that is required for those performing tamattu' and qiran during Hajj. The author explains that while other types of hady have no fixed time, these two types are strictly bound to the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). He also details the difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of early or delayed slaughter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation
Determine that the hady for tamattu' and qiran is wajib according to the Hanafi school, and that it has both a time and place restriction.
Other hady, like voluntary or penalty, are not time-bound.
2
State the time restriction
According to Abu Hanifa, the hady must be slaughtered on the day of Nahr (10th). If slaughtered after the days of Nahr, it suffices but the wajib is abandoned. Before the day of Nahr, it is invalid by consensus.
The Sahibayn consider slaughter before Nahr as makruh but valid, and after tahlil (shaving) there is no liability.
3
State the place restriction
All hady must be slaughtered within the Haram (Mecca precincts). An exception is the vowed badanah (camel), which according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is not restricted to the Haram.
Abu Yusuf analogizes the badanah to a vowed hady and requires the Haram.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf
Compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on timing, and the disagreement on the vowed badanah. Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
The mufta bihi for timing is Abu Hanifa's view; for badanah, the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text

للقدوري. وأراد المصنف النحر وقته وهو الأيام بيوم الثلاثة، وأراد بالاختصاص الاختصاص من حيث الوجوب على قول أبي حنيفة وإلا لو ذبح بعد أيام النحر أجزأ إلا أنه تارك للواجب وقبلها لا يجزئ بالإجماع، وعلى تقيد بالحرم اتفاقاً. كذا في المحيط. وقوله «لا بفقيره» بيان لجواز التصدق على فقراء غير الحرم بلحم الهدي لإطلاق الدلائل لكن التصدق على فقراء مكة أفضل كما في البدائع معزياً إلى الأصل قوله : (ولا يجب الهدي. والجلال جمع الجل وهو ما يلبس على الدابة والخطام هو الزمام وهو ما يجعل في أنف البعير لحديث البخاري مرفوعاً أن علياً رضي الله عنه أمره عليه السلام أن يقوم على بدنه وأن يقسم بدنه كلها لحومها لا يجوز، وإنما جاز له حالة الضرورة لما رواه صاحب السنن مرفوعاً اركبها بالمعروف إذا ألجئت إليها حتى تجد ظهراً» وفي الصحيح اركبها ويلك» في الثانية أو الثالثة حين رآه مضطراً إلى ركوبها. وفي جامع الترمذي «ويحك» أو «ويلك». وفي البدائع : ويحك كلمة ترحم وويلك كلمة تهدد وعلل الإمام الناصحي في الجمع بين وقفي هلال والخصاف بأن البدنة باقية على ملك صاحبها فيجوز الانتفاع بها عند الضرورة، ولهذا لو مات قبل أن أجرته الخ ) قال ابن الهمام وليس له بيع شيء من لحوم الهدايا فإن باع شيئاً أو أعطى الجزار أجره منه فعليه أن يتصدق بقيمته. وقال الطرابلسي : ولا يعطى أجرة الجزار منها ؛ فإن أعطى صار الكل لحماً لأنه إذا كلامهم أنها إن بركوبه الخ) تابعه في النهر وتعقبه في الشرنبلالية بأن المصرح به خلافه. قال في الجوهرة : ومن ساق بدنة فاضطر إلى ركوبها فإن ركبها أو حمل عليها متاعه ونقص منها شيء ضمن النقصان وتصدق به وإذا استغنى عنها لم يركبها .ا.هـ. وكذا صرح البرجندي بقوله : ولا يركب إلا لضرورة بأن كان عاجزاً عن المشي، وإذا ركبها وانتقص بركوبه فعليه ضمان ما نقص من ذلك ا هـ. وكذا صرح في الهداية بقوله : وإن استغنى عن ذلك لم يركبها إلا أن يحتاج إلى ركوبها، ولو ركبها فانتقص بركوبه فعليه ضمان ما نقص من ذلك اهـ. ومثله في كافي النسفي ومثله في الفتح عن كافي البحر الرائق/ ج ٣/ ٩٥
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Hady: And tamattu' and qiran only, and he specified slaughter of the hady of tamattu' and qiran on the day of Nahr only, and all are in the Haram, not to its poor. Explanation that the hady is restricted to place, whether it is blood of thanks or penalty, because it is defined as what is offered from cattle to the Haram. As for its restriction to time, it is specific to hady of tamattu' and qiran; the rest of the offerings are not restricted to time. And it indicates that voluntary hady, when it reaches the Haram, is not restricted to time, and this is correct, though slaughtering it on the day of Nahr is better, contrary to al-Quduri. The author meant by 'Nahr' its time, which is the days of the three, and by 'specification' he meant specification in terms of obligation according to Abu Hanifa; otherwise, if he slaughtered after the days of Nahr, it suffices but he is leaving the obligatory, and before them it does not suffice by consensus, and according to them (the two companions) similarly. The before and during are the sunnah according to them, so that if he slaughtered after tahlil by shaving, nothing is upon him, while according to him there is blood. Included under his saying 'and all in the Haram' is the vowed hady, contrary to the vowed badanah, which is not restricted to the Haram according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf said it is not permissible to slaughter it outside the Haram by analogy to vowed hady, and the difference is apparent. And they agreed that if he vowed to slaughter a camel or cow, it is not restricted to the Haram, and if he vowed a badanah from the symbols of Allah or intended to slaughter it in Mecca, it is restricted to the Haram by agreement. Thus in al-Muhit. And his saying 'not to its poor' is an explanation of the permissibility of giving in charity to the poor of other than the Haram from the meat of hady due to the generality of evidences, but giving in charity to the poor of Mecca is better, as in al-Badai' attributed to al-Asl. His saying: 'And it is not obligatory to make the hady known' because the hady indicates the transfer to the place of drawing near through shedding blood, not making it known, so it is not obligatory, and it is taking it to Arafat or publicizing by placing a garland and incising. And he did not mention its recommendation because there is detail: what is blood of thanks, it is recommended to make it known; what is blood of expiation, it is recommended to conceal it because its cause is an offense, like making up a prayer, it is recommended to conceal it. The author did not mention the sunnas of slaughter here because it is clear. His saying: 'And he gives in charity its saddlecloth and its nose string, and he does not give the wage of the butcher from it' meaning the hady. Al-jilal is plural of jull, which is what is worn on the animal; al-khatam is the nose string, which is what is placed on the camel's nose, due to the hadith of Bukhari marfu' that Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, the Prophet commanded him to take charge of his sacrificial animals and to distribute all of his sacrificial animals: their meat, skins, and saddlecloths, and not to give anything from them for butchering. And al-jizarah (with a damma on the jim) is the wage of the butcher's work. And it indicates that if he gives him from it his wage, he is liable for it because of destroying the meat or exchanging it. He specified 'wage' because if he gives in charity something of its meat to him besides his wage, it is permissible because he is eligible for charity. His saying: 'And he does not ride it without necessity' because he made it purely for the sake of Allah, so he does not benefit from anything of it. And it is explicitly stated in al-Muhit that riding it without need is haram, and it should be makruh tahrimi because the evidence is not decisive. And he indicated that he also does not load it, and that if he rides it or loads it and it decreases, he is liable for the decrease and gives it in charity to the poor, not to the rich, because the permissibility of benefiting from it for the rich is contingent upon reaching the destination. And it is absolute, so it includes what is permissible to eat and what is not. It is only permissible for him in case of necessity due to what is narrated by the compiler of the Sunan marfu': 'Ride it appropriately when you are forced to do so until you find a mount.' And in al-Sahih: 'Ride it, woe to you' the second or third time when he saw him forced to ride it. And in Jami' al-Tirmidhi: 'Wayhaka' or 'Waylaka'. And in al-Badai': 'Wayhaka' is a word of mercy, 'Waylaka' is a word of threat. And Imam al-Nasihi explained in the collection between the waqf of Hilal and al-Khassaf that the badanah remains the property of its owner, so it is permissible to benefit from it in necessity, and for this, if he dies before it reaches, it is inheritance. End. And apparently from their words that if it decreases due to his riding out of necessity, there is no liability upon him. His saying: 'And he does not milk it' meaning the hady, because it is part of it, so it is not permissible for him or for any other rich person, for if he milks it... His saying: '(And it indicates that if he gives him from it his wage...)' Ibn al-Humam said: And he does not have the right to sell anything of the meat of the hadaya; if he sells something or gives the butcher his wage from it, he must give in charity its value. And al-Tarabulusi said: And he does not give the butcher's wage from it; if he gives, the whole becomes meat because if he stipulates giving it to him, he remains a partner in it, so the whole is not permissible because of his intention for the meat; and if he gives without stipulation before slaughter, he is liable; and if he gives in charity something of it to him other than the wage, it is permissible if he is eligible for charity, as in Sharh al-Lubab. His saying: '(And apparently from their words that if it decreases due to his riding...' Al-Nahr followed him, and it was refuted in al-Sharnablaliyyah by stating that what is explicitly stated is contrary to this. Al-Jawharah said: He who drives a badanah and is forced to ride it, and rides it or loads his belongings on it and it decreases, he is liable for the decrease and gives it in charity; and when he becomes free of need, he does not ride it. End. Al-Barjandi also stated: And he does not ride except for necessity, such as being unable to walk; and if he rides it and it decreases due to his riding, he is liable for the decrease from it. End. Al-Hidayah also states: And if he becomes free of need, he does not ride it unless he needs to ride it; and if he rides it and it decreases due to his riding, he is liable for the decrease from it. End. Similar in Kafi al-Nasafi and similar in al-Fath from Kafi. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, vol. 3, p. 95.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq concerning the rulings specific to the sacrificial animal (hady) in Hajj. The author  explains several key points in sequence.

First, regarding the timing and place of slaughter: The hady for tamattu' and qiran must be slaughtered specifically on the day of Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah) according to Abu Hanifa, but if slaughtered after the days of Nahr it suffices while leaving a wajib; slaughter before Nahr is invalid by consensus. For other types of hady (voluntary, vowed, penalty), there is no time restriction, though it is best to slaughter on the day of Nahr. All hady must be slaughtered within the Haram (Mecca precincts). A vowed badanah (camel) is an exception: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is not restricted to the Haram, while Abu Yusuf analogizes it to a vowed hady and requires the Haram. However, if one vows a badanah as a 'symbol of Allah' or intends to slaughter in Mecca, it becomes restricted by agreement.

Second, the meat of the hady can be given in charity to poor Muslims anywhere, not only to the poor of the Haram, though giving it in Mecca is better.

Third, there is no obligation to 'define' the hady (i.e., take it to Arafat or mark it openly). For a voluntary (shukr) hady, defining is recommended; for an expiatory (kaffarah) hady, it is recommended to conceal it.

Fourth, the saddlecloth and nose string of the animal must be given in charity, based on the hadith of Ali. The butcher's wage must not be given from the hady itself; if one does so, he must compensate by giving the value in charity. However, giving other meat from the hady to the butcher as charity (not as wage) is permissible.

Fifth, one may not ride or load the sacrificial animal unless in dire necessity (e.g., unable to walk). If damage occurs from such use without necessity, the owner must compensate the loss and give it in charity. There is a dispute among later scholars whether compensation is due even in necessity; the dominant view in the later texts (like al-Jawharah and al-Hidayah) is that liability still applies, while some hold no liability. Milking the animal is also prohibited for the owner or any wealthy person.

Throughout, the author cites various Hanafi authorities (al-Muhit, al-Badai', al-Hidayah, etc.) and resolves apparent contradictions, such as the different wordings in copies regarding the negation 'la' in the matn.

Key Terms
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal brought to the Haram for offering, whether obligatory or voluntary.
المتعة (al-tamattu'): Performing 'Umrah during Hajj season and then Hajj in the same year with a single journey, requiring a hady.
القران (al-qiran): Combining Hajj and 'Umrah in one ihram, requiring a hady.
النحر (al-nahr): The day of Nahr, the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a pilgrim performing tamattu' slaughters his hady on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah, what is the ruling?
A) Invalid, must repeat.
B) Valid, no issues.
C) Valid but leaves a wajib.
D) Invalid, but can be compensated with charity.

Key Takeaway
The hady for tamattu' and qiran must be slaughtered within the days of Nahr and in the Haram; before the day of Nahr invalidates according to the mufta bihi view.

intermediate
8 min
Charity and Prohibited Transactions from the Hady
Commentary on charity and financial restrictions related to hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules regarding giving in charity from the hady (meat, jilal, khatam) and the prohibition of paying the butcher's wage from the animal.

Core Idea
The hady must be given fully in charity; its saddlecloth and halter belong to the poor, and the butcher's wage cannot be taken from its meat.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the financial obligations tied to the hady. The author explains that the meat of the hady can be given to the poor anywhere, but the saddlecloth and nose string must be given in charity specifically. Most importantly, the butcher may not be compensated from the animal itself; doing so requires compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the charity rules for meat
The meat of the hady can be given in charity to any poor Muslim, not only the poor of the Haram, though giving in Mecca is better.
This is based on the generality of evidences.
2
Identify the charity rules for jilal and khatam
The saddlecloth (jilal) and nose string (khatam) must be given in charity, based on the hadith that the Prophet commanded Ali to distribute them.
They cannot be kept by the owner.
3
Understand the prohibition on paying the butcher
The butcher's wage (jizarah) must not be given from the hady itself. If given, the owner becomes liable for the value of the meat given as wage.
An exception: if the meat is given as charity to the butcher (not as wage), it is permissible.
4
Apply the hadith evidence
The hadith of Ali (in Bukhari) explicitly states: 'Do not give anything for butchering.' This is the primary proof for the prohibition.
The imperative form ('la yu'ta') indicates prohibition.

Source Text

كتاب الحج باب الهدي والمتعة والقران فقط وخص ذبح هدى المتعة والقرآن بيوم النحر فقط والكل بالحرم لا بفقيره. بيان لكون الهدي موقتاً بالمكان سواء كان دم شكر أو جناية لما تقدم أنه اسم لما يهدى من النعم إلى الحرم. وأما توقيته بالزمان فمخصوص بهدي المتعة والقران وأما بقية الهدايا فلا تتقيد بزمان. وأفاد أن هدي التطوع إذا بلغ الحرم لا يتقيد بزمان وهو الصحيح، وإن كان ذبحه يوم النحر أفضل كما ذكره الشارح خلافاً للقدوري. وأراد المصنف النحر وقته وهو الأيام بيوم الثلاثة، وأراد بالاختصاص الاختصاص من حيث الوجوب على قول أبي حنيفة وإلا لو ذبح بعد أيام النحر أجزأ إلا أنه تارك للواجب وقبلها لا يجزئ بالإجماع، وعلى قولهما كذلك. القبلية وكونه فيها هو السنة عندهما حتى لو ذبح بعد التحلل بالحلق لا شيء عليه، وعنده فيه دم. ودخل تحت قوله والكل «بالحرم الهدي المنذور بخلاف البدنة المنذورة فإنها لا تتقيد بالحرم عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : لا يجوز ذبحها في غير الحرم قياساً على الهدي المنذور والفرق ظاهر واتفقوا على أنه لو نذر نحر جزور أو بقرة فإنه لا يتقيد بالحرم ولو نذر بدنة من شعائر الله أو نوى أن تنحر بمكة تقيد بالحرم اتفاقاً. كذا في المحيط. وقوله «لا بفقيره» بيان لجواز التصدق على فقراء غير الحرم بلحم الهدي لإطلاق الدلائل لكن التصدق على فقراء مكة أفضل كما في البدائع معزياً إلى الأصل قوله : (ولا يجب التعريف بالهدى) لأن الهدي ينبئ عن النقل إلى مكان التقرب بإراقة الدم فيه لا عن التعريف فلا يجب وهو الذهاب به إلى عرفات أو التشهير بالتقليد والإشعار ولم يذكر استحبابه لأن فيه تفصيلاً، فما كان دم شكر استحب تعريفه وما كان دم كفارة استحب إخفاؤه وستره لأن سببها الجناية كقضاء الصلاة يستحب إخفاؤه، ولم يذكر المصنف سنن الذبح والنحر هنا لما هو صريح. قوله : (ويتصدق بجلاله وخطامه ولم يعط أجر الجزار منه) أي الهدي. والجلال جمع الجل وهو ما يلبس على الدابة والخطام هو الزمام وهو ما يجعل في أنف البعير لحديث البخاري مرفوعاً أن علياً رضي الله عنه أمره عليه السلام أن يقوم على بدنه وأن يقسم بدنه كلها لحومها وجلودها وجلالها ولا يعطي في جزارتها شيئاً. وهي بضم الجيم كراء عمل الجزار. وأفاد أنه إن أعطاه منها أجرته ضمنه لإتلاف اللحم أو معاوضته. وقيد بالأجر لأنه لو تصدق بشيء من لحمها عليه سوى أجرته جاز لأنه أهل للصدقة عليه قوله : (ولا بركبه بلا ضرورة لأنه جعله خالصاً لوجه الله تعالى فلا ينتفع بشيء منه . وصرح في المحيط بأن ركوبه لغير حاجة حرام، وينبغي أن يكون مكروهاً كراهة تحريم لأن الدليل ليس قطعياً. وأشار إلى أنه لا يحمل عليها أيضاً وإلى أنه لو ركبها أو حمل عليها فنقصت فعليه ضمان ما نقص ويتصدق به على الفقراء دون الأغنياء لأن جواز الانتفاع بها للأغنياء معلق ببلوغ المحل. وأطلقه فشمل ما يجوز الأكل منه وما لا يجوز، وإنما جاز له حالة الضرورة لما رواه صاحب السنن مرفوعاً اركبها بالمعروف إذا ألجئت إليها حتى تجد ظهراً» وفي الصحيح اركبها ويلك» في الثانية أو الثالثة حين رآه مضطراً إلى ركوبها. وفي جامع الترمذي «ويحك» أو «ويلك». وفي البدائع : ويحك كلمة ترحم وويلك كلمة تهدد وعلل الإمام الناصحي في الجمع بين وقفي هلال والخصاف بأن البدنة باقية على ملك صاحبها فيجوز الانتفاع بها عند الضرورة، ولهذا لو مات قبل أن تبلغ كانت ميراثاً .اهـ. وظاهر كلامهم أنها إن نقصت بركوبه لضرورة فإنه لا ضمان عليه . قوله : (ولا يجلبه) أي الهدي لأنه جزؤه فلا يجوز له ولا لغيره من الأغنياء فإن حلبه قوله : (وأفاد إنه إن أعطاه منها أجرته الخ ) قال ابن الهمام وليس له بيع شيء من لحوم الهدايا فإن باع شيئاً أو أعطى الجزار أجره منه فعليه أن يتصدق بقيمته. وقال الطرابلسي : ولا يعطى أجرة الجزار منها ؛ فإن أعطى صار الكل لحماً لأنه إذا شرط أعطاه منه يبقى شريكاً له فيها فلا يجوز الكل لقصده اللحم، وإن أعطاه من غير شرط قبل الذبح ضمنه، وإن تصدق بشيء منها عليه من غير الأجرة جاز إن كان أهلاً للتصدق عليه كذا في شرح اللباب قوله : (وظاهر كلامهم أنها إن بركوبه الخ) تابعه في النهر وتعقبه في الشرنبلالية بأن المصرح به خلافه. قال في الجوهرة : ومن ساق بدنة فاضطر إلى ركوبها فإن ركبها أو حمل عليها متاعه ونقص منها شيء ضمن النقصان وتصدق به وإذا استغنى عنها لم يركبها .ا.هـ. وكذا صرح البرجندي بقوله : ولا يركب إلا لضرورة بأن كان عاجزاً عن المشي، وإذا ركبها وانتقص بركوبه فعليه ضمان ما نقص من ذلك ا هـ. وكذا صرح في الهداية بقوله : وإن استغنى عن ذلك لم يركبها إلا أن يحتاج إلى ركوبها، ولو ركبها فانتقص بركوبه فعليه ضمان ما نقص من ذلك اهـ. ومثله في كافي النسفي ومثله في الفتح عن كافي البحر الرائق/ ج ٣/ ٩٥

His saying: '(And apparently from their words that if it decreases due to his riding...' Al-Nahr followed him, and it was refuted in al-Sharnablaliyyah by stating that what is explicitly stated is contrary to this. Al-Jawharah said: He who drives a badanah and is forced to ride it, and rides it or loads his belongings on it and it decreases, he is liable for the decrease and gives it in charity; and when he becomes free of need, he does not ride it. End. Al-Barjandi also stated: And he does not ride except for necessity, such as being unable to walk; and if he rides it and it decreases due to his riding, he is liable for the decrease from it. End. Al-Hidayah also states: And if he becomes free of need, he does not ride it unless he needs to ride it; and if he rides it and it decreases due to his riding, he is liable for the decrease from it. End. Similar in Kafi al-Nasafi and similar in al-Fath from Kafi. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, vol. 3, p. 95.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq concerning the rulings specific to the sacrificial animal (hady) in Hajj. The author  explains several key points in sequence.

First, regarding the timing and place of slaughter: The hady for tamattu' and qiran must be slaughtered specifically on the day of Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah) according to Abu Hanifa, but if slaughtered after the days of Nahr it suffices while leaving a wajib; slaughter before Nahr is invalid by consensus. For other types of hady (voluntary, vowed, penalty), there is no time restriction, though it is best to slaughter on the day of Nahr. All hady must be slaughtered within the Haram (Mecca precincts). A vowed badanah (camel) is an exception: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is not restricted to the Haram, while Abu Yusuf analogizes it to a vowed hady and requires the Haram. However, if one vows a badanah as a 'symbol of Allah' or intends to slaughter in Mecca, it becomes restricted by agreement.

Second, the meat of the hady can be given in charity to poor Muslims anywhere, not only to the poor of the Haram, though giving it in Mecca is better.

Third, there is no obligation to 'define' the hady (i.e., take it to Arafat or mark it openly). For a voluntary (shukr) hady, defining is recommended; for an expiatory (kaffarah) hady, it is recommended to conceal it.

Fourth, the saddlecloth and nose string of the animal must be given in charity, based on the hadith of Ali. The butcher's wage must not be given from the hady itself; if one does so, he must compensate by giving the value in charity. However, giving other meat from the hady to the butcher as charity (not as wage) is permissible.

Fifth, one may not ride or load the sacrificial animal unless in dire necessity (e.g., unable to walk). If damage occurs from such use without necessity, the owner must compensate the loss and give it in charity. There is a dispute among later scholars whether compensation is due even in necessity; the dominant view in the later texts (like al-Jawharah and al-Hidayah) is that liability still applies, while some hold no liability. Milking the animal is also prohibited for the owner or any wealthy person.

Throughout, the author cites various Hanafi authorities (al-Muhit, al-Badai', al-Hidayah, etc.) and resolves apparent contradictions, such as the different wordings in copies regarding the negation 'la' in the matn.

Key Terms
الجلال (al-jilal): The saddlecloth or covering placed on the back of the sacrificial animal.
الخطام (al-khatam): The nose string or halter of the camel.
الجزارة (al-jizarah): The wage or fee paid to the butcher for slaughtering and cutting the meat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim pays the butcher's wage from the meat of the hady, what must he do?
A) Nothing, it is permissible.
B) He must compensate by giving the value of that meat in charity.
C) He must repeat the slaughter.
D) He must give the butcher a separate animal.

Key Takeaway
The saddlecloth and halter of the hady must be given to the poor, and the butcher's wage cannot be taken from the animal; if violated, compensation is due.

Prohibited Personal Use of the Hady and the Vowed Badanah Dispute
Commentary on prohibitions of using the hady and the vowed badanah dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibitions on riding, loading, and milking the hady, the exception of necessity, and the liability for damage, as well as the disagreement on the vowed badanah's place restriction.

Core Idea
You may not use the hady for personal benefit (riding, loading, milking) except in dire necessity, and a vowed badanah is generally not restricted to the Haram unless intended for Mecca.

This lesson covers the final set of rules from the passage: the restrictions on the owner's use of the sacrificial animal. The hady is consecrated to Allah, so one cannot ride it, load it, or milk it without necessity, and if damage occurs, compensation is required. Additionally, we revisit the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a vowed badanah (camel) must be slaughtered in the Haram, which was introduced in the first lesson.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The hady is made purely for Allah, so the owner cannot benefit from it personally. This includes riding, loading, and milking.
The prohibition applies to both obligatory and voluntary animals once they are designated.
2
Apply the exception of necessity
If the owner is forced (e.g., cannot walk), he may ride the animal or load it, but if it gets damaged, there is a dispute among later scholars about liability.
The hadith allows riding when forced, but liability for damage may still apply.
3
Determine liability for damage
According to al-Hidayah and most later texts, if the animal decreases in value due to riding (even for necessity), the owner must compensate the loss and give it in charity.
Some earlier texts exempt liability in cases of genuine necessity.
4
Understand the milking prohibition
Milking is prohibited because the milk is part of the animal and is for the poor; the owner or any rich person cannot consume it.
If milked, the milk must be given in charity.
5
Analyze the vowed badanah dispute
Recall from Lesson 1: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that a vowed badanah (camel) is not restricted to the Haram, while Abu Yusuf analogizes it to vowed hady and requires the Haram.
The practical consequence is where the animal may be slaughtered.

Book of Hajj, Chapter of Hady: And tamattu' and qiran only, and he specified slaughter of the hady of tamattu' and qiran on the day of Nahr only, and all are in the Haram, not to its poor. Explanation that the hady is restricted to place, whether it is blood of thanks or penalty, because it is defined as what is offered from cattle to the Haram. As for its restriction to time, it is specific to hady of tamattu' and qiran; the rest of the offerings are not restricted to time. And it indicates that voluntary hady, when it reaches the Haram, is not restricted to time, and this is correct, though slaughtering it on the day of Nahr is better, contrary to al-Quduri. The author meant by 'Nahr' its time, which is the days of the three, and by 'specification' he meant specification in terms of obligation according to Abu Hanifa; otherwise, if he slaughtered after the days of Nahr, it suffices but he is leaving the obligatory, and before them it does not suffice by consensus, and according to them (the two companions) similarly. The before and during are the sunnah according to them, so that if he slaughtered after tahlil by shaving, nothing is upon him, while according to him there is blood. Included under his saying 'and all in the Haram' is the vowed hady, contrary to the vowed badanah, which is not restricted to the Haram according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf said it is not permissible to slaughter it outside the Haram by analogy to vowed hady, and the difference is apparent. And they agreed that if he vowed to slaughter a camel or cow, it is not restricted to the Haram, and if he vowed a badanah from the symbols of Allah or intended to slaughter it in Mecca, it is restricted to the Haram by agreement. Thus in al-Muhit. And his saying 'not to its poor' is an explanation of the permissibility of giving in charity to the poor of other than the Haram from the meat of hady due to the generality of evidences, but giving in charity to the poor of Mecca is better, as in al-Badai' attributed to al-Asl. His saying: 'And it is not obligatory to make the hady known' because the hady indicates the transfer to the place of drawing near through shedding blood, not making it known, so it is not obligatory, and it is taking it to Arafat or publicizing by placing a garland and incising. And he did not mention its recommendation because there is detail: what is blood of thanks, it is recommended to make it known; what is blood of expiation, it is recommended to conceal it because its cause is an offense, like making up a prayer, it is recommended to conceal it. The author did not mention the sunnas of slaughter here because it is clear. His saying: 'And he gives in charity its saddlecloth and its nose string, and he does not give the wage of the butcher from it' meaning the hady. Al-jilal is plural of jull, which is what is worn on the animal; al-khatam is the nose string, which is what is placed on the camel's nose, due to the hadith of Bukhari marfu' that Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, the Prophet commanded him to take charge of his sacrificial animals and to distribute all of his sacrificial animals: their meat, skins, and saddlecloths, and not to give anything from them for butchering. And al-jizarah (with a damma on the jim) is the wage of the butcher's work. And it indicates that if he gives him from it his wage, he is liable for it because of destroying the meat or exchanging it. He specified 'wage' because if he gives in charity something of its meat to him besides his wage, it is permissible because he is eligible for charity. His saying: 'And he does not ride it without necessity' because he made it purely for the sake of Allah, so he does not benefit from anything of it. And it is explicitly stated in al-Muhit that riding it without need is haram, and it should be makruh tahrimi because the evidence is not decisive. And he indicated that he also does not load it, and that if he rides it or loads it and it decreases, he is liable for the decrease and gives it in charity to the poor, not to the rich, because the permissibility of benefiting from it for the rich is contingent upon reaching the destination. And it is absolute, so it includes what is permissible to eat and what is not. It is only permissible for him in case of necessity due to what is narrated by the compiler of the Sunan marfu': 'Ride it appropriately when you are forced to do so until you find a mount.' And in al-Sahih: 'Ride it, woe to you' the second or third time when he saw him forced to ride it. And in Jami' al-Tirmidhi: 'Wayhaka' or 'Waylaka'. And in al-Badai': 'Wayhaka' is a word of mercy, 'Waylaka' is a word of threat. And Imam al-Nasihi explained in the collection between the waqf of Hilal and al-Khassaf that the badanah remains the property of its owner, so it is permissible to benefit from it in necessity, and for this, if he dies before it reaches, it is inheritance. End. And apparently from their words that if it decreases due to his riding out of necessity, there is no liability upon him. His saying: 'And he does not milk it' meaning the hady, because it is part of it, so it is not permissible for him or for any other rich person, for if he milks it... His saying: '(And it indicates that if he gives him from it his wage...)' Ibn al-Humam said: And he does not have the right to sell anything of the meat of the hadaya; if he sells something or gives the butcher his wage from it, he must give in charity its value. And al-Tarabulusi said: And he does not give the butcher's wage from it; if he gives, the whole becomes meat because if he stipulates giving it to him, he remains a partner in it, so the whole is not permissible because of his intention for the meat; and if he gives without stipulation before slaughter, he is liable; and if he gives in charity something of it to him other than the wage, it is permissible if he is eligible for charity, as in Sharh al-Lubab. His saying: '(And apparently from their words that if it decreases due to his riding...' Al-Nahr followed him, and it was refuted in al-Sharnablaliyyah by stating that what is explicitly stated is contrary to this. Al-Jawharah said: He who drives a badanah and is forced to ride it, and rides it or loads his belongings on it and it decreases, he is liable for the decrease and gives it in charity; and when he becomes free of need, he does not ride it. End. Al-Barjandi also stated: And he does not ride except for necessity, such as being unable to walk; and if he rides it and it decreases due to his riding, he is liable for the decrease from it. End. Al-Hidayah also states: And if he becomes free of need, he does not ride it unless he needs to ride it; and if he rides it and it decreases due to his riding, he is liable for the decrease from it. End. Similar in Kafi al-Nasafi and similar in al-Fath from Kafi. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, vol. 3, p. 95.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq concerning the rulings specific to the sacrificial animal (hady) in Hajj. The author  explains several key points in sequence.

First, regarding the timing and place of slaughter: The hady for tamattu' and qiran must be slaughtered specifically on the day of Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah) according to Abu Hanifa, but if slaughtered after the days of Nahr it suffices while leaving a wajib; slaughter before Nahr is invalid by consensus. For other types of hady (voluntary, vowed, penalty), there is no time restriction, though it is best to slaughter on the day of Nahr. All hady must be slaughtered within the Haram (Mecca precincts). A vowed badanah (camel) is an exception: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is not restricted to the Haram, while Abu Yusuf analogizes it to a vowed hady and requires the Haram. However, if one vows a badanah as a 'symbol of Allah' or intends to slaughter in Mecca, it becomes restricted by agreement.

Second, the meat of the hady can be given in charity to poor Muslims anywhere, not only to the poor of the Haram, though giving it in Mecca is better.

Third, there is no obligation to 'define' the hady (i.e., take it to Arafat or mark it openly). For a voluntary (shukr) hady, defining is recommended; for an expiatory (kaffarah) hady, it is recommended to conceal it.

Fourth, the saddlecloth and nose string of the animal must be given in charity, based on the hadith of Ali. The butcher's wage must not be given from the hady itself; if one does so, he must compensate by giving the value in charity. However, giving other meat from the hady to the butcher as charity (not as wage) is permissible.

Fifth, one may not ride or load the sacrificial animal unless in dire necessity (e.g., unable to walk). If damage occurs from such use without necessity, the owner must compensate the loss and give it in charity. There is a dispute among later scholars whether compensation is due even in necessity; the dominant view in the later texts (like al-Jawharah and al-Hidayah) is that liability still applies, while some hold no liability. Milking the animal is also prohibited for the owner or any wealthy person.

Throughout, the author cites various Hanafi authorities (al-Muhit, al-Badai', al-Hidayah, etc.) and resolves apparent contradictions, such as the different wordings in copies regarding the negation 'la' in the matn.

Key Terms
البدنة (al-badanah): A camel (or cow) that is offered as a sacrifice, often used as a mount or carrier.
بلا ضرورة (bila darurah): Without necessity, i.e., when one is not forced by inability to walk or other pressing need.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, if a pilgrim rides his hady camel due to necessity and the camel is damaged, what must he do?
A) Nothing, because necessity permits it.
B) He must give the camel to the poor as a penalty.
C) He must compensate the decrease in value and give it in charity.
D) He must sacrifice the camel immediately.

Key Takeaway
The hady is consecrated; personal use is prohibited except in necessity, and compensation is required for any damage, even from necessary use.

Charity of the Coverings and Prohibition of Wages from the Hady
Commentary on the matn's ruling on coverings and wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on the hady's coverings and wages, apply the hadith of 'Ali, and explain the consequence of violating the prohibition.

Core Idea
The hady's coverings belong to Allah — they must be given in charity, and wages cannot come from the animal itself.

This lesson unpacks the matn's ruling on the hady: its coverings and halter are to be donated, and the slaughterer's wage cannot be taken from its meat. The commentator cites a famous hadith and explores the liability if these rules are broken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn ruling
Read the matn phrase: 'ويتصدق بجلاله وخطامه ولم يعط أجرة الجزار منه'. Understand that the cover (jull) and halter (khitam) must be given in charity, and wages for slaughter must not be given from the animal.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The commentator cites the hadith of 'Ali: the Prophet ordered all parts of the hady, including covers, be distributed in charity and nothing given for slaughtering. Identify the legal implications: the command indicates obligation (wujub) for charity and prohibition (tahrim) for wages.
Hadith is in Bukhari; thubut is zanni, but relied upon.
3
Analyze the wage ruling
The text states that if wages are given from the hady, the giver becomes liable (daman) for the value. Understand the reason: it is either considered a wasteful consumption of a devoted item or a prohibited exchange (mu'awada).
4
Distinguish between wages and charity
The commentator notes that giving charity from the hady to the slaughterer (other than his wage) is permissible if he is eligible for charity. Recognize that the prohibition is specific to wages as compensation for the work.

كتاب الحج باب الهدي بفقيره ولا يجب التعريف بالهدى ويتصدق بجلاله وخطامه ولم يعط أجر الجزار منه ولا به في باب الذبائح والأضحية قوله : ( ويتصدق بجلاله وخطامه ولم يعط أجرة الجزار منه) أي الهدي. والجلال جمع الجل وهو ما يلبس على الدابة والخطام هو الزمام وهو ما يجعل في أنف البعير لحديث البخاري مرفوعاً أن علياً رضي الله عنه أمره عليه السلام أن يقوم على بدنه وأن يقسم بدنه كلها لحومها وجلودها وجلالها ولا يعطي في جزارتها شيئاً. وهي بضم الجيم كراء عمل الجزار. وأفاد أنه إن أعطاه منها أجرته ضمنه لإتلاف اللحم أو معاوضته. وقيد بالأجر لأنه لو تصدق بشيء من لحمها عليه سوى أجرته جاز لأنه أهل للصدقة عليه قوله : (ولا بركبه بلا ضرورة لأنه جعله خالصاً لوجه الله تعالى فلا ينتفع بشيء منه . وصرح في المحيط بأن ركوبه لغير حاجة حرام، وينبغي أن يكون مكروهاً كراهة تحريم لأن الدليل ليس قطعياً. وأشار إلى أنه لا يحمل عليها أيضاً وإلى أنه لو ركبها أو حمل عليها فنقصت فعليه ضمان ما نقص ويتصدق به على الفقراء دون الأغنياء لأن جواز الانتفاع بها للأغنياء معلق ببلوغ المحل. وأطلقه فشمل ما يجوز الأكل منه وما لا يجوز، وإنما جاز له حالة الضرورة لما رواه صاحب السنن مرفوعاً اركبها بالمعروف إذا ألجئت إليها حتى تجد ظهراً» وفي الصحيح اركبها ويلك» في الثانية أو الثالثة حين رآه مضطراً إلى ركوبها. وفي جامع الترمذي «ويحك» أو «ويلك». وفي البدائع : ويحك كلمة ترحم وويلك كلمة تهدد وعلل الإمام الناصحي في الجمع بين وقفي هلال والخصاف بأن البدنة باقية على ملك صاحبها فيجوز الانتفاع بها عند الضرورة، ولهذا لو مات قبل أن تبلغ كانت ميراثاً .اهـ. وظاهر كلامهم أنها إن نقصت بركوبه لضرورة فإنه لا ضمان عليه . نقصت
قوله : (ولا يجلبه) أي الهدي لأنه جزؤه فلا يجوز له ولا لغيره من الأغنياء فإن حلبه
قوله : (وأفاد إنه إن أعطاه منها أجرته الخ ) قال ابن الهمام وليس له بيع شيء من لحوم الهدايا فإن باع شيئاً أو أعطى الجزار أجره منه فعليه أن يتصدق بقيمته. وقال الطرابلسي : ولا يعطى أجرة الجزار منها ؛ فإن أعطى صار الكل لحماً لأنه إذا شرط أعطاه منه يبقى شريكاً له فيها فلا يجوز الكل لقصده اللحم، وإن أعطاه من غير شرط قبل الذبح ضمنه، وإن تصدق بشيء منها عليه من غير الأجرة جاز إن كان أهلاً للتصدق عليه كذا في شرح اللباب قوله : (وظاهر كلامهم أنها إن بركوبه الخ) تابعه في النهر وتعقبه في الشرنبلالية بأن المصرح به خلافه. قال في الجوهرة : ومن ساق بدنة فاضطر إلى ركوبها فإن ركبها أو حمل عليها متاعه ونقص منها شيء ضمن النقصان وتصدق به وإذا استغنى عنها لم يركبها .ا.هـ. وكذا صرح البرجندي بقوله : ولا يركب إلا لضرورة بأن كان عاجزاً عن المشي، وإذا ركبها وانتقص بركوبه فعليه ضمان ما نقص من ذلك ا هـ. وكذا صرح في الهداية بقوله : وإن استغنى عن ذلك لم يركبها إلا أن يحتاج إلى ركوبها، ولو ركبها فانتقص بركوبه فعليه ضمان ما نقص من ذلك اهـ. ومثله في كافي النسفي ومثله في الفتح عن كافي البحر الرائق/ ج ٣/ ٩٥ 6
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Hady. It is not obligatory to announce the hady, and one gives charity of its covering and halter, and does not give the slaughterer's wage from it. He said: (And he gives charity of its covering and halter, and does not give the slaughterer's wage from it) meaning the hady. Al-Jilal is the plural of jull, which is what is put on the animal, and al-khitam is the halter, which is put in the nose of the camel, due to the hadith of Bukhari raised that Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) was commanded by the Prophet (peace be upon him) to supervise his sacrificial animals and to distribute all of his sacrificial animals: their meat, their skins, their covers, and not to give anything for their slaughtering. ...
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. It opens by stating rules regarding the hady (sacrificial animal) in Hajj. The commentator explains that the animal's covering and halter are to be given in charity, as supported by the hadith of 'Ali. Giving the slaughterer's wages from the animal is prohibited; if given, compensation is required. Riding the animal without necessity is forbidden (makruh tahrimi) because it is devoted to Allah. However, riding out of necessity is permitted based on a hadith, and if damage occurs, the rider must compensate for the loss. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding compensation when riding out of necessity: some early sources hold no liability, but later authoritative texts (al-Jawhara, al-Hidaya) state that compensation is due. The commentator leans towards the latter. The passage also touches on milking, but that is more fully addressed in the next section.

Key Terms
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal brought by a pilgrim to Mecca for the Hajj or Umrah.
الجلال (al-jilal): Plural of jull, the cover or cloth placed on the back of the sacrificial animal.
الخطام (al-khitam): The halter or rope placed in the nose of the camel used for leading.
أجرة الجزار (ujrat al-jazzar): The wage of the slaughterer for slaughtering the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if a pilgrim gives the slaughterer's wage from the meat of the hady?
A) The act is permissible and no compensation needed.
B) The pilgrim must compensate the value of what was given.
C) The hady becomes invalid and must be repeated.
D) The pilgrim must give the entire hady in charity again.

Key Takeaway
The hady's coverings must be given in charity, and the slaughterer's wage cannot be taken from the animal; violation requires compensation.

Riding the Hady: Necessity and Compensation
Commentary on the matn's ruling on riding the hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on riding the hady, identify the ikhtilaf regarding compensation, and apply the mufta bihi in practice.

Core Idea
Riding the hady is only allowed out of necessity, but even then, any damage must be compensated.

This lesson addresses the permissibility of riding the sacrificial animal (hady) during Hajj. The matn states it should not be ridden without necessity. The commentator expands with proofs, discusses the level of prohibition, and resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether compensation is due when riding out of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn ruling on riding
The matn says: 'ولا بركبه بلا ضرورة' — it is not to be ridden without necessity. Understand that riding is ordinarily prohibited.
2
Determine the level of prohibition
The commentator classifies the prohibition as makruh tahrimi (close to haram) because the evidence (ahad hadith) is not decisive. Recognize that this is a Hanafi technical distinction: the act is sinful but not as severe as haram.
Hanafi usul: imperatives and prohibitions from ahad hadith yield wujub/tahrim only if the meaning is clear; otherwise, it is makruh tahrimi.
3
Understand the exception for necessity
Riding out of necessity (idhtirar) is permitted based on a hadith: 'Ride it with kindness when forced.' The commentator cites this to show the basis for the exception.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf on compensation
Some early Hanafi texts suggest no liability for damage when riding out of necessity (zahir kalam). However, later authoritative sources (al-Jawhara, al-Hidaya) insist that compensation is due for any deficiency. The commentator sides with the latter, stating that the animal's devoted nature requires restitution.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is the view requiring compensation.

الضمان (al-daman): Liability or compensation for loss or damage.
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity that overrides a prohibition, such as inability to walk or lack of alternative transport.

Rulings on Milking, Sprinkling, and Disabled Hady
Rulings on milking, sprinkling, and disabled hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on sprinkling the udder, milking, and the replacement of defective obligatory hady, distinguishing between obligatory and voluntary hady.

Core Idea
An obligatory hady must be replaced if disabled; a voluntary hady is slaughtered locally and marked.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies several practical issues related to the hady (sacrificial animal) during Hajj. It covers the recommended act of sprinkling the udder with cold water before slaughter, the permissibility of milking if the slaughter is delayed, and the critical distinction between obligatory and voluntary hady when the animal becomes disabled or defective. The underlying principle is that an obligatory hady is a debt upon the pilgrim, while a voluntary hady becomes a sacrifice at the place of disablement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings on sprinkling and milking
First, locate the statements about sprinkling the udder with 'al-nuqakh' (cold water) and the condition of when to milk. Understand the recommended timing: close to slaughter or far from it.
The text says sprinkling is done if close to slaughter; if far, the animal is milked and the milk is given in charity.
2
Distinguish obligatory vs voluntary hady when disabled or defective
Note the two categories: 'wajib' (obligatory, e.g., for tamattu' or qiran) and 'tatawwu' (voluntary). For wajib, if the animal dies (al-atab) or becomes defective (al-ayb), it must be replaced. For voluntary, it is slaughtered at that location.
The word 'atab' means actual death for wajib and near-death for voluntary.
3
Examine the dalil for replacement of wajib hady
The text compares it to zakat: if zakat money is lost before distribution, it must be replaced. The obligation is in the dhimmah (liability), so the specific animal is not fixed.
This is a qiyas (analogy) to the principle of debt being in the liability.
4
Apply the ruling to the voluntary hady: local slaughter and marking
For a voluntary hady that is disabled, it is slaughtered locally, its sandal is dyed with its blood, and its side is struck. The wealthy are prohibited from eating it; only the poor may eat.
This marks it as a hady so people know it is for sacrifice.

Page 130: Book of Hajj, Chapter of Hady. He does not ride it without necessity, nor does he milk it, and he sprinkles its udder with cold water. Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the Hady chapter. It covers several distinct rulings: (1) The udder of the hady is sprinkled with cold water shortly before slaughter to prevent engorgement; if the time is far, the animal is milked and the milk given in charity. (2) If an obligatory hady (wajib, e.g., due to tamattu') becomes disabled (dies) or defective (has a fault that prevents validity), it must be replaced, and the defective animal becomes the owner's personal property. This is because the obligation is in the liability (dhimmah), not on a specific animal. (3) If it is a voluntary hady (nafl), it is slaughtered locally, its blood is applied as a mark, and only the poor eat from it. (4) Garlanding (taqleed) is only sunnah for a camel of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran, not for the hady of ihsar or penalties. The proofs are based on the principle that the hady is devoted to Allah and specific rules apply.

Key Terms
النقاخ (al-nuqakh): Cold, fresh water that refreshes the heart, used to sprinkle the udder.
العطب (al-atab): Disablement approaching death or actual death of the hady.
الذمة (al-dhimmah): Liability or legal responsibility; the location of the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for an obligatory hady that becomes disabled (dies) before reaching the Haram?
A) The pilgrim is excused; no replacement needed.
B) The pilgrim must replace it with another hady.
C) The pilgrim must sacrifice the dead animal as is.
D) The pilgrim must free the animal if it is still alive.

Key Takeaway
An obligatory hady is a debt in the liability; if the designated animal is lost or defective, it must be replaced, while a voluntary hady is sacrificed locally.

Garlanding the Hady: When It Is Sunnah
Ruling on garlanding hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of hady are garlanded (taqleed) according to the Hanafi school and state the reason for the distinction.

Core Idea
Only the camel of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran hady is garlanded; not for penalty or ihsar hady.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq continues the commentary on the rulings of hady by specifying which animals are to be garlanded (taqleed). The author clarifies that garlanding is only a sunnah for the camel of voluntary hady, tamattu' hady, and qiran hady, not for the hady of ihsar (being prevented from completing Hajj) or for penalty hady (dam al-jinayat). The reasoning is tied to the purpose of garlanding: it is a form of display (izhar) and publicity (tashhir) suitable for a devotional sacrifice, whereas for penalties and ihsar, concealment is more appropriate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals subject to taqleed
Note the phrase: 'only the hady of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran are garlanded'. Recognize that it is restricted to camels (badanah) and not sheep or goats.
The text specifies 'badanah' (camel) because garlanding is not sunnah for smaller animals.
2
Examine the types excluded: ihsar and penalties
The hady of ihsar (compensation for being prevented) and dam al-jinayat (penalties for violations) are not garlanded. The reason given: concealment (sitr) is more fitting because these are compensatory (jabirah) or due to a violation.
The text says 'the hady of ihsar is compensatory, so it follows its kind (penalties).'
3
Understand the wisdom behind the distinction
Garlanding is a way to publicly mark the animal as a sacrifice. For voluntary and ritual hady, display enhances the devotion. For penalties, discretion is better to avoid humiliation.
If someone garlands an excluded type, it is still valid (no harm), but the sunnah is not to do so.

Rulings for Defective Wajib vs Voluntary Hady
Rulings for handling defective, riding, milking, and garlanding of hady animals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on defective wajib and voluntary hady animals and explain the ta'lil (reasoning) behind the distinction.

Core Idea
A wajib hady must be substituted if defective because the obligation is on the dhimma; a voluntary hady is slaughtered in place and given in charity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, details the proper treatment of sacrificial animals (hady) during Hajj. It distinguishes between wajib (obligatory) and tatawwu' (voluntary) animals, providing different procedures when they become crippled or defective. The reasoning (ta'lil) centres on whether the obligation is attached to the animal itself or to the owner's liability (dhimma). We will work through the rulings step by step, covering riding, milking, garlanding, and what to do with the animal's milk, offspring, and proceeds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial prohibitions
The passage begins by stating that one should not ride or milk the hady without necessity. This applies to all hady animals. Determine the legal status: is it haram, makruh, or permissible under duress?
Riding without necessity is prohibited; milking is allowed only if the udder is engorged, and even then, the milk should be given in charity.
2
Differentiate between wajib and tatawwu' animals
Classify the hady as either wajib (e.g., vowed, tamattu', qiran) or tatawwu' (voluntary). This classification determines the ruling when the animal becomes defective (aṭaba or taʿayyaba).
Wajib animals: the obligation is in the dhimma. Tatawwu': the animal is owned and dedicated for a purpose.
3
Apply the substitution rule for wajib animals
If a wajib animal is destroyed or becomes defective (e.g., breaks a leg), a substitute must be offered. The original animal becomes the owner's property. Trace the reasoning: 'because the obligation is on the dhimma, so it does not fall until slaughtered in its place'.
The passage analogizes this to zakat dirhams that are lost before distribution.
4
Apply the slaughter-and-mark rule for tatawwu' animals
If a voluntary animal is crippled (near destruction, not actual destruction), it is slaughtered and marked by dyeing its sandal/collar with blood. The owner does not eat from it, nor the rich. Understand the benefit: people recognize it as hady so the poor eat.
The permission to consume is conditional upon reaching the destination; slaughtering early is better than leaving it for beasts.
5
Examine subsidiary rulings: garlanding, milk, offspring
Only voluntary camels and those for tamattu' and qiran are garlanded (taqlid). Not for ihsar or violations. Also, if milked, the milk must be given in charity; if the animal gives birth, the offspring is similarly disposed of. If one uses the animal (rides, milks for self), he is liable for the diminution in value.
Garlanding is a sunnah for camels to display the hady; sheep are not garlanded.

He does not ride it without necessity, nor milk it, and he sprinkles its udder with cold water. And if an obligatory (wajib) animal becomes crippled or defective, he substitutes another for it, and the defective one is his. And if it is a voluntary (tatawwu') animal, he slaughters it, dyes its sandal with its blood, strikes its flank with it, and does not eat from it, and the rich man does not eat from it. And only a voluntary badanah (camel), and that of tamattu' and qiran, is garlanded. If he uses it or gives it to a rich person, he is liable for it because of transgression, just as if he did that with its fur or wool. In al-Muhit: he is liable for its value, making milk a fungible. In Ghayat al-Bayan: he is liable for its like or its value. And if he does not use it after milking, he gives it in charity to the poor. And it is indicated that if it gives birth, he gives it in charity or slaughters it with it. If he consumes it, he is liable for its value; if he sells it, he gives its price in charity; and if he buys a hady with it, that is good. His statement: (and he sprinkles its udder with cold water) meaning he sprays it with cold water until it contracts. An-nuqakh (with dammah on the nun, qaf, and kha') is fresh water that cools the heart, as in al-Sihah and al-Mughrib. In al-Misbah al-Munir: it is from the two patterns of daraba and nafa'a, so its dad is kasrah or fatha. They said: this is when it is near the time of slaughter, but if it is far, he milks it and gives its milk in charity so that it does not harm it. And his statement: (And if an obligatory animal becomes crippled or defective, he substitutes another for it, and the defective one is his) because what is obligatory is in the liability (dhimma), so it does not fall from him until he slaughters it in its place. What is meant by 'crippled' here is destruction, from the verb 'alima, so it is like if he set aside dirhams of zakat and they were destroyed before distribution to the poor, then he must give them again. What is meant by 'defective' is what prevents sacrifice, so it is like its destruction. And the defective one is only his because he had dedicated it for a purpose, and that purpose has been nullified, so it remains his property. And does this include under 'obligatory' the case where he vowed a specific sheep and it perished, so he must substitute another? Or not, because the obligation is on the specific animal, not on the liability? His statement: (And if it is voluntary, he slaughters it, dyes its sandal with its blood, strikes its flank with it, and does not eat from it, and the rich man does not eat) meaning even if the crippled or defective animal is a voluntary one, he slaughters it and dyes its collar with its blood. What is meant by 'crippled' here is near destruction, not destruction. The benefit of this act is that people know it is a hady, so the poor eat from it but not the rich. This is because permission to consume it is conditional upon it reaching its place, so it is not permissible before that at all, except that giving in charity to the poor is better than leaving it as meat for beasts, and there is a kind of devotion in it, and devotion is the goal. His statement: (And only a voluntary badanah, and that of tamattu' and qiran, is garlanded) because it is the blood of a ritual, and garlanding displays and publicizes it, so it is fitting. By saying 'only', he indicates that the blood of ihsar and the blood of violations are not garlanded because their cause is violation, and concealment is more suitable; and the blood of ihsar is compensatory, so it follows its kind. If he garlands it, it does not harm him, as in al-Mabsut. And he restricted to badanah because garlanding a sheep is not sunnah, nor is it customarily garlanded. And voluntary includes vowed animals because when it is obligated by the servant, it is voluntary, i.e., not initially obligated by the Lawgiver. So it is mentioned in the context of ritual and worship. If you say: it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) garlanded the animals of ihsar, the answer is that he had garlanded them for tamattu', then when he was prevented (ihsar), they remained as they were, so they were sent to Mecca. As in al-Muhit: he garlands the blood of a vow because it is the blood of the ruler. He said: if he rides it or loads his luggage on it out of necessity, he is liable for what it diminished, i.e., if it diminished it, he is liable for it. End.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rulings for sacrificial animals (hady) in the Hanafi school. It is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author first addresses the proper treatment: one should not ride or milk the animal unnecessarily, but may sprinkle its udder with cold water to reduce milk. If the animal is obligatory (wajib, e.g., a vowed animal) and becomes crippled or defective, a substitute must be offered; the defective animal becomes the owner's property. For voluntary animals, one slaughters it and marks it by dyeing the sandal or collar with blood, so people recognize it as a hady; the rich may not eat from it. Only a camel (badanah) for voluntary, tamattu', or qiran is garlanded; not for ihsar or violations. The commentary provides linguistic notes and cites sources like al-Muhit and Ghayat al-Bayan. It distinguishes between complete loss and near-loss, and discusses liability if one uses the animal. The reasoning (ta'lil) is based on the obligation being in the dhimma (liability) for wajib animals, while voluntary animals are owned and can be disposed of charitably.

Key Terms
عطب (aṭaba): In this passage, 'atab' means destruction or near-destruction of the animal.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal brought to the Haram during Hajj or Umrah.
تقلد (taqlīd): To put a garland or something on the animal's neck to mark it as a hady.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if a wajib (obligatory) hady animal becomes defective (e.g., breaks a leg)?
A) Slaughter it and give the meat to the poor.
B) Substitute another animal in its place, and the defective one becomes his property.
C) Release it and it is no longer required.
D) Eat it himself because it is now his.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between wajib and tatawwu' hady determines the procedure when the animal becomes defective: wajib must be substituted, tatawwu' is slaughtered and given in charity.

Testimony on Standing at Arafat: Istihsan vs. Qiyas
Ruling on testimony about wuqoof before or after the day.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts testimony of wuqoof on the day of Tarwiyah using istihsan and distinguish between acceptance of testimony and validation of the act.

Core Idea
Acceptance of testimony does not equal validation; istihsan overrides qiyas to avoid hardship.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling on accepting testimony that pilgrims stood at Arafat on the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah) before the actual day. The Hanafi school, using istihsan, accepts such testimony to prevent hardship, even though strict analogy would reject it. We will explore the evidence, the ikhtilaf, and the practical implications for pilgrims and judges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State what the passage rules: testimony of standing before the day of Arafah is accepted; testimony after is not. Also, standing alone (not with the imam) invalidates.
The ruling has two parts: acceptance of testimony and validity of standing.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith 'I made Arafat known to you on the day you recognise' and the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj).
Also note the use of istihsan over qiyas.
3
Follow the Ikhtilaf
Understand the two views in al-Hidayah: (1) testimony not accepted because it is negation, (2) testimony accepted but does not validate standing. The second is preferred.
The opposing view (qiyas) rejects acceptance altogether.
4
Note the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: if testimony is accepted, the imam hears it but does not declare the Hajj valid; the pilgrims may need to repeat standing if it was wrong.
The imam may also refuse to hear it to avoid fitna.

Scattered issues: And if they testify about their standing (wuqoof) before its day, it is accepted, and after it, not. And if he leaves the first jamrah on that day, its situation is such. Likewise in Ghayat al-Bayan. And he did not mention the time of taqlid because there is detail: if he sends it, he garlands it from his country, and if he is with him, lack of sunnah. So from where he enters ihram... Scattered issues are established in some copies but not others. The practice of authors is that they mention at the end of the book what is rare and scattered from previous chapters in a separate section to increase benefits, and they say at its beginning: 'Scattered issues' or 'Miscellaneous issues' etc. His statement: 'And if they testify about their standing before its day, it is accepted, and after it, not.' That is, if they testify after people have stood at Arafat that they stood on the day of Tarwiyah, their testimony is accepted; and if they testify that they stood on the day of Nahr, it is not accepted. The analogy is that it does not suffice them, considering the case if they stood on the day of Tarwiyah. This is because it is an act of worship specific to time and place, so worship does not occur without them. It is mentioned in al-Hidayah regarding istihsan that there are two aspects: first, that it is not accepted because it is a testimony of negation; second, that it is accepted but does not necessitate the validity of the standing, because this type of confusion is prevalent and cannot be avoided. If the permissibility was not judged after ijtihad, extreme hardship would follow, which is negated by Shariah, and this is the wisdom of his saying (peace be upon him): 'I made Arafat known to you on the day you recognise', meaning the time of standing at Arafat in the sight of Allah is the day on which people stand based on ijtihad and their opinion that it is the day of Arafah. In Mi'raj al-Dirayah, it is mentioned that the second aspect is more correct. And he favoured it in Fath al-Qadir by refuting the first because it is based on actual affirmation, i.e., sighting the crescent on the night before the sighting by the people of the standing, so it is not testimony of negation. And since such testimony does not establish the validity of standing, there is no benefit for the imam in hearing it, so he does not hear it, because hearing it would publicize it among the common people of the standing, increasing gossip and causing fitna, and disturbing the hearts of Muslims with doubt about their Hajj after their long hardship. So when they come to testify, he tells them: 'Go away, I do not hear the testimony. The people's Hajj is complete, and likewise the Hajj of the witnesses.' If they stood alone, it does not suffice them, and they must repeat standing with the imam due to the previous hadith. Likewise, if the imam delays the standing in a way that allows ijtihad, the standing of those who stood before him is not valid. The muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir found it difficult to picture the acceptance of testimony in the first issue because there is no doubt that their standing on the day of Tarwiyah as the ninth is not contradicted... (text cut off)
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with scattered issues (masa'il manthurah) commonly added at the end of fiqh books. The main ruling discussed is about accepting testimony regarding wuqoof (standing at Arafat). If witnesses testify that they stood on the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah) before the actual day of Arafah, their testimony is accepted because it is based on their sighting of the crescent. But if they testify that they stood on the day of Nahr (10th) as if it were Arafah, it is not accepted. The Hanafi school uses istihsan (juristic preference) to accept the first testimony, even though analogy would reject it, to avoid hardship. The author cites al-Hidayah and Fath al-Qadir, noting that the second opinion (accepted but does not necessitate validity) is preferred by later scholars. The reason for not accepting the second testimony is to prevent fitna and doubt among the pilgrims. The passage also mentions that those who stood alone (not with the imam) must repeat wuqoof, and if the imam delays the standing, earlier standing is invalid. The text ends abruptly but covers the core ruling.

Key Terms
مسائل منثورة (masā'il manthūrah): Scattered issues; a section at the end of a fiqh book containing miscellaneous rulings not covered in earlier chapters.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; departing from strict analogy to avoid hardship or achieve a better outcome.
الحرج (al-ḥaraj): Hardship; a principle that Shariah does not impose unbearable difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He rejects the testimony because it is a negation of correct timing.
B) He accepts the testimony and declares their Hajj valid.
C) He accepts the testimony but does not necessarily validate their standing.
D) He ignores them because they are lying.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony of wuqoof on the day of Tarwiyah using istihsan, but this acceptance is separate from the validity of the standing itself.
