Vow to Perform Hajj on Foot Requires Walking Until Tawaf al-Rukn
Explains that a vow to perform Hajj walking obligates walking until the essential tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a vow to perform Hajj walking and explain the extent of the obligation to walk.

Core Idea
A vow to walk Hajj obligates walking until tawaf al-rukn; after that, riding is permitted.

Sometimes a person makes a vow (nathr) to perform Hajj on foot, meaning they will walk during the rituals. But what exactly is required? The Hanafi school, based on Imam Muhammad's transmission in al-Jami' al-Saghir, clarifies that the obligation to walk extends only until the essential tawaf (tawaf al-rukn). After that, one may ride. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its textual basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a vow to perform Hajj on foot. The ruling is that the person may not ride until he performs tawaf al-rukn.
The text explicitly says 'la yarkabu hatta yatufa lil-rukn'.
2
Understand the legal basis
The text states that this expression comes from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad, which reports the speech of Abu Hanifa, establishing the ruling as part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
Zahir al-Riwayah carries strong authority in the Hanafi school.
3
Determine the limit of obligation
The obligation to walk ends at tawaf al-rukn. This is the essential circumambulation that is a pillar of Hajj. After performing it, riding is permissible.
Tawaf al-rukn occurs at the end of Hajj, after stoning the jamarat and sacrifice.
4
Note the textual correction
The commentator corrects a grammatical point: the word 'wajib' should be in the nominative case, not accusative, as per al-Fath and other copies.
This illustrates the care in transmitting the exact wording of the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومن أوجب حجاً ماشياً لا يركب حتى يطوف للركن) أي بأن نذر الحج ماشياً وفيه إشارة إلى وجوب المشي لأن عبارة المختصر عبارة الجامع الصغير وهي كلام المجتهد أعني أبا حنيفة رضي الله تعالى عنه على ما نقله محمد عنه فيه وهو إخبار المجتهد وإخباره الوقوف بمجرد الظن مستحيل في هذا الموقف العظيم، وقالوا غلبة الظن منزلة منزلة اليقين فيحمل عليه. كذا في الشرنبلالية قوله : أن يكون من جنس المنذور (واجباً كذا في الفتح. والنسخ التي رأيتها وصوابه «واجب» بالرفع
His saying: (And whoever obligates himself to Hajj on foot, he may not ride until he performs tawaf for the rukn.) That is, if he vows to perform Hajj walking. It contains an indication of the obligation of walking because the expression of al-Mukhtasar is the expression of al-Jami' al-Saghir, and it is the speech of the mujtahid, meaning Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him), as transmitted by Muhammad from him in it, and it is the report of the mujtahid. And his report: 'Wukuf based on mere assumption is impossible in this great station, and they said: Preponderance of assumption is placed in the rank of certainty, so it is carried upon it.' Likewise in al-Shurnubalaliyyah. His saying: 'That it be of the same kind as the vowed (obligatory).' Likewise in al-Fath. And the copies I have seen, and its correct form is 'wajib' in the nominative case.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage deals with a vow (nathr) to perform Hajj on foot. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states: 'Whoever obligates himself to Hajj on foot may not ride until he performs the essential tawaf (tawaf al-rukn).' The commentator explains that this ruling is derived from the fact that the expression in the matn comes from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad, which reports the statement of Abu Hanifa. The phrase 'hajjan mashiyan' (Hajj on foot) itself indicates the obligation to walk. However, the exact extent of walking is limited: he must walk until he performs the tawaf al-rukn (the obligatory tawaf of Hajj). After that, he may ride if needed. The text then includes a side note about the impossibility of standing at 'Arafah based on mere assumption, emphasizing that preponderant assumption (ghalabat al-zann) is treated like certainty in the matter of determining the day of 'Arafah. The final part addresses a textual correction: the phrase 'an yakuna min jins al-mandhur' should be read as 'wajib' in the nominative, as per al-Fath and other copies.

Key Terms
نذر (nathr): A vow to perform an act of worship, making it obligatory upon oneself
ماشياً (mashiyan): Walking on foot, as distinguished from riding
طواف الركن (tawaf al-rukn): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba that is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj, without which Hajj is incomplete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, until what point must one walk if he vows to perform Hajj on foot?
A) Until he reaches Mina
B) Until he finishes stoning the jamarat
C) Until he performs the essential tawaf (tawaf al-rukn)
D) Until he completes all rituals including sa'y

Key Takeaway
A vow to perform Hajj on foot obligates walking only until the essential tawaf; after that, riding is permissible.

Conditions for Accepting Testimony on the Day of Arafah
Detailed analysis of testimony acceptance during Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi conditions for accepting testimony about the day of Arafah when it contradicts the crowd's belief.

Core Idea
Testimony about the day of Arafah is accepted only if the Imam was assuming without proof and correction is still possible.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq addresses a nuanced dispute: when witnesses testify that the day is the 8th of Dhul Hijjah while the Imam and people believe it is the 9th. The general rule that testimony against established practice is rejected is qualified by the Hanafi school, which considers whether the Imam's belief was based on assumption and whether correction of the standing is feasible. The commentary expands on three scenarios, using qiyas and istihsan to determine acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Ruling
Recognize that the core issue is whether testimony that the day is the 8th (Tarwiyah) is accepted when the people are standing as if it is the 9th (Arafah).
The opposing view holds such testimony is never accepted.
2
Analyze the Imam's Basis
The Imam may be standing on an assumption (without confirmed moon sighting) or on confirmed sighting. The ruling depends on this distinction.
If the Imam had confirmed sighting, testimony contradicting is rejected.
3
Check Correction Possibility – Day or Night
Even if the Imam assumed, testimony is accepted only if the standing can still be performed correctly during the day (or night) with most people.
If correction is impossible, testimony is rejected.
4
Apply Istihsan for Night Standing
If the Imam can only stand with most people at night (not during the day), testimony is still accepted by istihsan.
This shows Hanafi flexibility to preserve the Hajj.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
If testimony is accepted but the Imam fails to correct the standing, the Hajj of those who followed the assumption is invalid.
Witnesses are treated like others in this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شهادة من شهد أنه الثامن لأن اعتقاد الثامن إنما يكون بناء على أن أول ذي الحجة ثبت بإكمال عدة ذي القعدة واعتقاده التاسع بناء على أنه رؤي قبل الثلاثين من ذي القعدة، فهذه شهادة على الإثبات والقائلون أنه الثامن حاصل ما عندهم نفي محض وهو أنهم لم يروه ليلة الثلاثين من ذي القعدة ورآه الذين شهدوا فهي شهادة لا معارض لها اهـ. فحاصله أن الشهادة على خلاف ما وقف الناس لا يثبت بها شيء مطلقاً، سواء كان قبله أو بعده. وهو إنما يتم أن لو انحصر التصوير فيما ذكره بل صورته لو وقف الإمام بالناس ظناً منه أنه يوم التاسع من غير أن يثبت عنده رؤية الهلال فشهد قوم أنه اليوم الثامن فقد تبين خطأ ظنه والتدارك ممكن فهي شهادة لا معارض لها. ولهذا قال في المحيط : لو وقفوا يوم التروية على ظن أنه يوم رفة لم يجزهم. وبهذا التقرير علم أن المسألة تحتاج إلى تفصيل ولا بدع فيه بل هو متعين. وقد بقي هنا مسألة ثالثة وهي ما إذا شهدوا يوم التروية والناس بمنى يوم عرفة ينظر؛ فإن أمكن الإمام أن يقف مع الناس أو أكثرهم نهاراً قبلت شهادتهم قياساً واستحساناً للتمكن من الوقوف فإن لم يقفوا عشية فاتهم الحج، وإن أمكنه أن يقف معهم ليلاً لا نهاراً فكذلك استحساناً، وإن لم يمكنه أن يقف ليلاً مع أكثرهم لا تقبل شهادتهم ويأمرهم أن يقفوا من الغد استحساناً، والشهود في هذا كغيرهم كما قدمناه. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : ولا ينبغي للإمام أن يقبل في هذا شهادة الواحد والاثنين ونحو ذلك
Testimony of one who testifies that it is the eighth [of Dhul Hijjah], because the belief that it is the eighth is based on the fact that the first of Dhul Hijjah was established by completing the count of Dhul Qa'dah, and his belief that it is the ninth is based on that it was sighted before the thirtieth of Dhul Qa'dah. So this is testimony of affirmation, and those who say it is the eighth, all they have is pure negation: that they did not see it on the night of the thirtieth of Dhul Qa'dah, and those who testified saw it, so it is testimony with no opposing evidence. So the conclusion is that testimony contrary to what the people are standing on does not establish anything absolutely, whether it is before or after. And this is only valid if the scenario is limited to what he mentioned. Rather, the scenario is: If the Imam stands with the people assuming it is the ninth without having established sighting of the moon, and then a group testifies that it is the eighth, then his assumption is proven wrong and correction is possible, so this is testimony with no opposing evidence. For this reason, Al-Muhit said: If they stood on the day of Tarwiyah assuming it was the day of 'Rafah' [?], it would not be valid for them. And by this explanation, it is known that the issue requires detail; it is not an innovation but rather necessary. And there remains here a third issue: If they testify on the day of Tarwiyah while the people are at Mina on the day of Arafah, it is to be considered. If the Imam is able to stand with the people or most of them during the day, their testimony is accepted by qiyas and istihsan because standing is possible; if they do not stand in the evening, their Hajj is invalid. If he can stand with them at night but not during the day, it is similar by istihsan. If he cannot stand at night with most of them, their testimony is not accepted and he orders them to stand the next day by istihsan. And witnesses in this matter are like others as we have mentioned. In Al-Fatawa al-Dhahiriyyah: The Imam should not accept in this the testimony of one or two persons and the like.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of a ruling regarding testimony about the day of Arafah. It begins by contrasting two scenarios: someone testifying that the day is the 8th (Tarwiyah) versus the 9th (Arafah). The author explains that the belief in the 8th is based on completing Dhul Qa'dah as 30 days, while the belief in the 9th is based on moon sighting before 30 days. The testimony here is affirmative, while the popular belief is a negation. The ruling is that such testimony does not establish anything if it contradicts what people are acting upon. However, the author refines this: if the Imam was merely assuming it is the 9th without confirmed sighting, and witnesses testify it is the 8th, their testimony proves his error and is accepted because correction is possible. The passage then introduces a third scenario: if testimony comes on Tarwiyah while people are at Mina on Arafah. The acceptance depends on whether the Imam can still join the standing with most people during the day or night. The Hanafi position is detailed with qiyas and istihsan. Finally, it notes that in this context, the Imam should not accept testimony from one or two witnesses only, as per Al-Fatawa al-Dhahiriyyah.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony or legal evidence given before a judge regarding the sighting of the moon for Dhul Hijjah.
يوم التروية (yawm al-tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul Hijjah, the day before Arafah, when pilgrims go to Mina.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a Hanafi method of reasoning that departs from strict qiyas for the sake of convenience or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is testimony that the day is the 8th of Dhul Hijjah accepted even though the people are standing as if it is the 9th?
A) Always, because it is affirmative testimony.
B) Only if the Imam had confirmed the moon sighting.
C) Only if the Imam was merely assuming and correction of the standing is possible.
D) Only if more than two witnesses testify.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law accepts corrective testimony about the day of Arafah if the Imam was assuming and the standing can still be performed correctly, using qiyas and istihsan.

Order of Stoning on the Second Day of Tashreeq
Ruling on omitting the first stoning on the second day of Tashreeq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of stoning on the second day of Tashreeq, explain why it is sunnah and not wajib, and distinguish it from acts where order is binding.

Core Idea
Order of stoning on second day is sunnah because each stoning is independent; wajib order requires a command, not just the Prophet's action.

This passage clarifies a common point of confusion in hajj rituals: the order of stoning the three jamarat on the second day of Tashreeq. Many pilgrims worry about missing a stoning and breaking the sequence. The text explains that the order is only sunnah, not wajib, and provides a clear legal distinction: order becomes binding only when established by a command (amr), not merely by the Prophet's action (fi'l).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is leaving the first stoning on the second day. The ruling: the order among the three stonings is sunnah, not wajib or a condition.
The text explicitly says 'ليس بشرط ولا واجب وإنما هو سنة'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof for the ruling is the Prophet's action (fi'l) of stoning in order, not a verbal command.
Hadith of the Prophet's practice of stoning sequentially.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates recommendation (sunnah), not obligation, unless there is evidence that it was done to show obligation. Here, no such evidence exists.
Contrast with commands (amr) which indicate wajib.
4
Note the contrasts with other acts
The text contrasts with sa'y before tawaf and tawaf before standing at Arafah, where order is binding because established by text (amr or ijma). Also contrasts with starting sa'y from Marwah, which is established by a clear command.
These contrasts strengthen the sunnah ruling by showing when order is wajib.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the fact that each stoning is an independent act of worship; no text makes one dependent on another. Therefore, the order is sunnah and omitting the first stoning does not require repeating the sequence.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو ترك الجمرة الأولى في اليوم الثاني رمى الثلاث أو الأولى فقط بيان لكون الترتيب في الجمار الثلاث في اليوم الثاني ليس بشرط ولا واجب وإنما هو سنة ولهذا قدم قوله «رمى الثلاث» لمراعاة الترتيب المسنون لأن كل جمرة قربة قائمة بنفسها لا تعلق لها بغيرها وليس بعضها تابعاً لبعض بخلاف السعي قبل الطواف أو الطواف قبل الوقوف فإنه شرع مرتباً على وجه اللزوم فلم يدخل وقته، ولولا ورود النص في قضاء الفوائت بالترتيب قلنا لا يلزم فيها أيضاً لأن كل صلاة عبادة مستقله، وبخلاف البداءة بالمروة لأن البداءة من الصفا ثبت بالنص وهو قوله عليه السلام «ابدؤوا بما بدأ الله به بصيغة الأمر بخلاف الترتيب في الجمار الثلاث فإنه ثبت بالفعل وهو لا يفيد أكثر السنة .
His saying: (And if he leaves the first stoning on the second day, he stones the three or the first only) is an explanation that order in the three stonings on the second day is not a condition nor obligatory, but rather sunnah. For this reason he prefaced his saying 'he stones the three' to observe the recommended order, because each stoning is an act of worship standing by itself, not related to others, and none is dependent on another. Unlike sa'y before tawaf or tawaf before standing (at Arafah), for these are legislated in a binding order, so they do not enter their time unless done in order. And were it not for the text regarding making up missed prayers in order, we would say that order is not necessary there either, because each prayer is an independent act of worship. And unlike starting with al-Marwah, because starting from al-Safa is established by text in his saying (peace be upon him): 'Begin with what Allah began with' in the imperative mood, unlike order in the three stonings, which is established by action (fi'l), which does not give more than sunnah.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn (كنز الدقائق) regarding the ruling on leaving the first stoning on the second day of Tashreeq. The author explains that the order of stoning the three jamarat on that day is not a condition (shart) nor obligatory (wajib), but rather a sunnah (recommended). Each stoning is an independent act of worship; they are not interdependent. The text then contrasts this with other acts where order is binding: sa'y before tawaf, and tawaf before standing at Arafah. For these, the order is essential and the acts cannot be performed out of sequence. Also, making up missed prayers require order due to a specific text. Similarly, starting sa'y from al-Safa is established by a command (amr), whereas the order of stonings is only established by the Prophet's action (fi'l), which indicates sunnah, not obligation. Therefore, if someone omits the first stoning, they can either stone all three in order (recommended) or just the first stoning alone; the order is not mandatory.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act; omission is not sinful but contrary to optimal practice.
ترتيب (tartīb): Specific order of performing the three stonings sequentially.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is the order of stoning on the second day not wajib?
A) Because each stoning is an independent act of worship.
B) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) never did it.
C) Because it is established by command (amr).
D) Because stoning is not a required act.

Key Takeaway
The order of stoning the three jamarat on the second day is sunnah, not wajib, because it is established by the Prophet's action, not by a command.

Vow to Perform Hajj on Foot
Rulings on one who vows to walk during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for one who vows to walk during Hajj, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the mufta bihi position to determine where walking begins and what compensation is due if riding occurs.

Core Idea
A vow to walk during Hajj makes walking wajib; riding requires compensation but does not invalidate the vow.

This lesson examines the rulings for one who vows to perform Hajj on foot. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the obligation of walking, the intra-Hanafi differences, and the practical details of where to begin and what happens if one rides. Understanding this ensures the vow is fulfilled correctly according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position from al-Jami' al-Saghir
Identify the core ruling from the base text: walking is obligatory for one who vows to walk during Hajj. This is attributed to Abu Hanifa via Muhammad al-Shaybani's transmission.
The text uses 'awjaba' indicating obligation.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi opposing views
Note that Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut gives a choice between riding and walking, and another report from Abu Hanifa considers riding better. These represent legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
The dispute is on the level of obligation vs. permissibility.
3
Examine the evidence (dalil) for each view
Analyze the hadith about walking reward (supports obligation) and the hadith of 'Uqba's sister (used by those who allow riding with compensation). Understand how each proof is interpreted.
Both are ahad hadith, zanni al-thubut.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference) and its basis
Later scholars like Qadikhan and Fakhr al-Islam prefer the obligation because the vow is to perform the act in its perfect form (walking). The Prophet's permission in the hadith of 'Uqba's sister is treated as a specific exception (nass).
The principle 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applies: the intent is to walk.
5
Apply to practical details: start, end, and compensation
Determine where walking begins (three opinions; mufta bihi: from the house), where it ends (tawaf al-ziyarah), and what compensation is due if one rides (dam for most/all, sadaqah for a little).
Custom (urf) is considered in determining the start if not explicitly stated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومن أوجب حجاً ماشياً لا يركب حتى يطوف للركن) أي بأن نذر الحج ماشياً وفيه إشارة إلى وجوب المشي لأن عبارة المختصر عبارة الجامع الصغير وهي كلام المجتهد أعني أبا حنيفة رضي الله تعالى عنه على ما نقله محمد عنه فيه وهو إخبار المجتهد وإخباره معتبر بإخبار الشرع لأنه نائبه في بيان الأحكام كما في المعراج. وفي الأصل أي المبسوط : لمحمد أيضاً خيره بين الركوب والمشي، وعن أبي حنيفة أنه كره المشي فيكون الركوب أفضل . وصحح ما في الجامع الصغير قاضيخان في شرحه واختاره فخر الإسلام معللاً بأنه التزم القربة بصفة الكمال. وإنما قلنا إن المشي أكمل لما روي عن النبي أنه قال «من حج ماشياً كتب له بكل خطوة حسنة من حسنات الحرم. قيل وما حسنات الحرم؟ قال: واحدة بسبعمائة». وإنما رخص الشرع في الركوب دفعاً للحرج. قال في غاية البيان: ولا يرد عليه ما أورد في النوازل عن أبي حنيفة أن الحج راكباً أفضل لأن ذلك لمعنى آخر أن وهو المشي خلقه وربما يقع في المنازعة والجدال المنهي عنه وإلا فالأجر على قدر التعب والتعب في المشي أكثر اهـ . لا يقال لا نظير للمشي في الواجبات ومن شرط صحة النذر أن يكون من جنس المنذور واجباً لأنا نقول : بل له نظير وهو مشي المكي الذي لا يجد الراحلة وهو قادر على المشيء فإنه يجب عليه أن يحج ماشياً ونفس الطواف أيضاً، ولم يذكر المصنف محل وجوب ابتداء المشي لأن محمداً رحمه الله لم يذكره فلذا اختلف المشايخ فيه على ثلاثة أقوال : قيل من بيته وهو الأصح كذا في فتح القدير وغيره لأنه المراد عرفاً، وقيل من الميقات، وقيل من أي موضع يحرم منه واختاره فخر الإسلام والإمام العتابي وصححه في غاية البيان لأنه نذر بالحج والحج ابتداؤه الإحرام وانتهاؤه طواف الزيارة فيلزمه بقدر ما التزم. ولا عبرة مع وجود اللفظ بخلاف الوصية بالحج فإنه يحج عنه من بيته لأن الوصية تنصرف إلى الفرض في الأصل، ولهذا يحج عنه راكباً لا ماشياً والمعول عليه هو التصحيح الأول، ويدل عليه من الرواية ما عن أبي حنيفة لو أن بغدادياً قال إن كلمت فلاناً فعلي أن أحج ماشياً فلقيه بالكوفة فكلمه فعليه أن يمشي من بغداد وقوله لا عبرة بالعرف مع وجود اللفظ» ممنوع بل المعتبر في النذور والأيمان العرف لا اللفظ كما عرف في محله. وفي فتح القدير : ولو أحرم بالعرف من بيته فالاتفاق على أن يمشي من بيته وإنما ينتهي وجوب المشي بطواف الزيارة لأن به ينتهي الإحرام، وأما طواف الصدر فللتوديع وليس بأصل في الحج حتى لا يجب على من لا يودع. وأفاد بقوله لا يركب أنه لو ركب لزمه الجزاء لترك الواجب فإذا ترك في الكل أو في الأكثر يلزمه الدم وفي الأقل يلزمه التصدق بقدره من قيمة الشاة الوسط، ومقتضى الأصل أن لا يخرج عن عهدة النذر إذا ركب كما لو نذر الصوم متتابعاً فقطع التتابع ولكن في الحج فوجب العمل به وهو ما عن ابن عباس أن أخت عقبة نذرت أن تحج ماشية فأمرها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن تركب وتهدي دماً. رواه أبو داود. وهو محمول على أن ثبت ذلك نصاً.
His saying: (And whoever makes Hajj obligatory walking, he does not ride until he performs tawaf for the pillar) meaning he vows to perform Hajj walking. And it contains an indication of the obligation of walking because the wording of the Mukhtasar is the wording of al-Jami' al-Saghir, and it is the speech of the mujtahid, meaning Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him) as transmitted by Muhammad from him. And the report of a mujtahid is considered like the report of the Shari'ah because he is its deputy in explaining rulings as in al-Mi'raj. And in al-Asl (al-Mabsut) there is also from Muhammad that he gave him a choice between riding and walking, and from Abu Hanifa that he disliked walking, so riding is better. And Qadikhan in his commentary made sahih what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir, and Fakhr al-Islam chose it, explaining that he obligated the act of worship in its perfect form. We only say that walking is more perfect because of what is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: ‘Whoever performs Hajj walking, for every step he gets a hasanah from the hasanat of the Haram.’ It was asked: What are the hasanat of the Haram? He said: ‘One is equal to seven hundred.’ And the Shari'ah permitted riding to avoid hardship. He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: And it is not refuted by what was transmitted in al-Nawazil from Abu Hanifa that Hajj riding is better, because that is for another meaning: that walking may create his nature and perhaps leads to dispute and argument which is prohibited; otherwise, reward is according to exertion, and exertion in walking is more. It cannot be said that walking has no parallel in obligations and that the condition for validity of a vow is that the vowed act must be of the same genre as obligatory acts. We say: Rather it has a parallel, which is the walking of a Makkan who cannot find a mount and is able to walk, for it is obligatory upon him to perform Hajj walking, and also the circumambulation itself. And the author did not mention the place where the obligation of walking begins because Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention it; therefore the mashayikh differed into three opinions: It is said from his house, which is the most correct as in Fath al-Qadir and others because that is what is conventionally understood. And it is said from the miqat. And it is said from whichever place he enters ihram, chosen by Fakhr al-Islam and al-Imam al-Atabi and deemed sahih in Ghayat al-Bayan because he vowed Hajj, and the beginning of Hajj is ihram and its end is tawaf al-ziyarah, so it is incumbent upon him to the extent of what he vowed. And no consideration is given to custom when the wording is present, contrary to a will regarding Hajj, for the Hajj is performed from his house because the will refers to the original obligation, and for this reason it is performed riding not walking. And the relied-upon is the first correction, and it is supported by the narration from Abu Hanifa: If a Baghdadi said 'If I speak to so-and-so, then I am obliged to perform Hajj walking', and he meets him in Kufa and speaks to him, then he must walk from Baghdad. And his statement 'custom is not considered when wording exists' is rejected; rather, in vows and oaths, custom is considered, not wording, as known in its place. And in Fath al-Qadir: And if he enters ihram by custom from his house, there is agreement that he walks from his house. And the obligation of walking ends with tawaf al-ziyarah because the ihram ends with it. As for tawaf al-sadr, it is for farewell and is not a fundamental part of Hajj, so it is not obligatory upon one who does not say farewell. And his saying 'he does not ride' implies that if he rides, compensation is due for leaving the obligation. So if he leaves it entirely or mostly, blood (dam) is due; if he leaves it infrequently, he gives sadaqah to the extent of one-third of the value of a medium sheep. And the principle (mujtada al-asl) is that he does not exit from the liability of the vow by riding, just as if he vowed to fast consecutively and broke the consecutiveness. But in Hajj, it is obligatory to act on it, and that is what is from Ibn Abbas that the sister of 'Uqbah vowed to perform Hajj walking, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered her to ride and sacrifice a sheep (dam). Narrated by Abu Dawud. And it is interpreted as that was established by text.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling for one who vows to perform Hajj on foot. It opens by clarifying that the matn (from al-Jami' al-Saghir) indicates the obligation of walking, attributed to Abu Hanifa. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad al-Shaybani in al-Mabsut gives a choice between riding and walking, and Abu Hanifa reportedly disliked walking, making riding better. The preferred position is that walking is obligatory because one vowed the act in its perfect form. The text supports walking as more perfect with a hadith about multiplied rewards. Riding is permitted only to avoid hardship. The author then addresses an objection: that walking is not analogous to other obligations, but he gives the example of a Makkan who must walk if unable to ride. Next, the passage discusses where the walking must begin: three opinions – from one's house (the most correct according to Fath al-Qadir), from the miqat, or from the point of ihram. The relied-upon view is from the house, based on custom and a narration from Abu Hanifa. The passage emphasizes that custom is considered in vows, not literal wording. The obligation of walking ends with tawaf al-ziyarah. If one rides, compensation is required: for riding entirely or mostly, a dam (sacrifice) is necessary; for a little riding, sadaqah. The text also addresses the hadith of 'Uqba's sister where the Prophet allowed her to ride with a dam, explaining it as a specific textual permission.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship; it becomes wajib upon utterance.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) offered as compensation for leaving a wajib in Hajj.
طواف الزيارة (tawāf al-ziyārah): The essential circumambulation of the Ka'bah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah; also called tawaf al-ifadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, where does one who vows to perform Hajj walking begin walking?
A) From the miqat.
B) From the point of ihram.
C) From his house.
D) From the Ka'bah.

Key Takeaway
One who vows to walk to Hajj must walk from his house until tawaf al-ziyarah; if he rides, he must compensate with a dam for most of the journey or sadaqah for a little.

Walking in a Vow of Hajj: Virtue, Starting Point, and Penalties
Explains the virtue of walking vs. riding and where the obligation to walk begins in a vow

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the virtue of walking vs. riding in a vowed Hajj, identify the relied-upon starting point for the obligation to walk, and apply the rule to different vow wordings including the penalty for riding.

Core Idea
Walking in a vowed Hajj is more virtuous but riding is permitted; the obligation to walk begins from one's home, not the miqat.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the virtue of walking in a Hajj vow and the crucial dispute about where the obligation to walk begins. It also details the penalties for riding without excuse and extends to various vow wordings, distinguishing between binding and non-binding expressions. By the end, you will be able to articulate the Hanafi position and apply it to common vow scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on walking vs. riding
Determine whether walking is obligatory or merely virtuous in a vowed Hajj, and note the difference between Abu Hanifa's preference and the relied-upon view.
The hadith on reward shows virtue, not obligation.
2
Locate the dispute on the starting point of the obligation
Identify the three views: from home (relied-upon), from miqat, or from point of ihram. Understand the reasoning behind each.
The author supports home based on custom and a narration from Abu Hanifa.
3
Analyze the penalty for riding without excuse
Trace the consequence: if one rides, compensation varies — dam for most of the journey, charity for a small part. The hadith of Uqbah's sister shows riding with dam is allowed in case of inability.
This indicates walking is a wajib in the vow.
4
Apply the rule to ambiguous vow wordings
Work through examples: 'walking to the House' (obligates one ritual), 'to the Haram' (difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn), and non-binding wordings like 'to al-Safa'.
Custom plays a key role in interpretation.

والأيمان العرف لا اللفظ كما عرف في محله. وفي فتح القدير : ولو أحرم به من بيته فالاتفاق على أن يمشي من بيته وإنما ينتهي وجوب المشي بطواف الزيارة لأن ينتهي الإحرام، وأما طواف الصدر فللتوديع وليس بأصل في الحرام ولم يذكر حجاً ولا عمرة لزمه أحد النسكين استحساناً، فإن جعله عمرة مشى حتى يحلق إلا إذا نوى به المشي إلى مسجد المدينة أو مسجد بيت المقدس أو مسجد من المساجد فإنه لا يلزمه شيء. وقوله على المشي إلى مكة أو الكعبة» كقوله «إلى بيت الله ولو قال علي المشي إلى الحرم أو المسجد الحرام فإنه لا شيء عليه عند أبي حنيفة لعدم العرف بالتزام النسك به. وقالا : يلزمه النسك احتياطاً. واتفقوا على أنه لا لزوم لو قال إلى الصفا أو المروة أو مقام إبراهيم أو إلى أستار الكعبة أو بأبها أو ميزابها أو عرفات أو المزدلفة أو مسجد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، أو ذكر مكان المشي غيره كقوله «علي الذهاب إلى بيت الله» أو «الخروج».
It is considered valid by the informing of the Shari'ah because he is its deputy in explaining rulings as in al-Mi'raj. In al-Asl (i.e., al-Mabsut): Muhammad also gave him choice between riding and walking, and from Abu Hanifa that he disliked walking, so riding is better. What is in al-Jami' al-Saghir is corrected by Qadikhan in his commentary and chosen by Fakhr al-Islam, reasoning that he undertook worship with perfection. We only say that walking is more complete because of what is reported from the Prophet that he said: 'Whoever performs Hajj walking, for every step is written for him a good deed from the good deeds of the Sanctuary. It was asked: What are the good deeds of the Sanctuary? He said: One is multiplied seven hundred times.' The Shari'ah permitted riding to remove hardship. He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: The objection from al-Nawazil that Abu Hanifa said Hajj riding is better is not valid because that is for another meaning: that walking might cause argument and forbidden dispute; otherwise, reward is according to exertion, and exertion in walking is greater. It cannot be said that walking has no parallel in obligations and that validity of a vow requires the vowed act to be of the same type as an obligatory act, for we say: There is a parallel, which is the walking of a Meccan who does not find a mount and is able to walk; he must perform Hajj walking, and also the Tawaf itself. The author did not mention the place where walking becomes obligatory because Muhammad did not mention it; hence the scholars differed into three views: It is said from his home – which is the relied-upon view as in Fath al-Qadir and others because that is what is meant customarily; it is said from the Miqat; and it is said from any place from which he enters Ihram – chosen by Fakhr al-Islam and Imam al-Atabi and corrected in Ghayat al-Bayan because he vowed Hajj, and Hajj begins with Ihram and ends with Tawaf al-Ziyarah, so the obligation is to the extent of his commitment. No consideration is given to custom when a wording exists, unlike a bequest for Hajj, which is performed from his home because a bequest is directed to the obligatory Hajj originally, hence it is performed riding, not walking; the relied-upon view is the first correction. The narration from Abu Hanifa supports it: if a Baghdad resident said, 'If I speak to so-and-so, I must perform Hajj walking,' then he met him in Kufa and spoke, he must walk from Baghdad. His saying 'no consideration for custom with the existence of wording' is rejected; rather, in vows and oaths, custom is considered, not wording, as known in its place. In Fath al-Qadir: If he enters Ihram from his home, there is agreement that he must walk from his home; the obligation of walking ends with Tawaf al-Ziyarah because the Ihram ends; Tawaf al-Sadr is for farewell and is not fundamental to Hajj, so it is not obligatory on one who does not perform it. He indicated by his statement 'he should not ride' that if he rides, he must pay a penalty for omitting an obligatory act: if he omits it entirely or for most of the journey, he must sacrifice a dam (blood), and for a small part, he must give charity equal to that part from the value of a medium sheep. The implication of the principle is that he does not fulfill his vow if he rides, just as if he vowed to fast consecutively and interrupted the consecutiveness, but in Hajj, the ruling is based on action, which is what Ibn Abbas reported: that the sister of Uqbah vowed to perform Hajj walking, so the Messenger of Allah ﷺ ordered her to ride and sacrifice a dam (blood). Reported by Abu Dawud. It is interpreted as her inability to walk, indicated by another narration that she could not endure it. And he stated generally in the obligation, so it includes whether it is immediate or conditional, and whether he said 'for Allah upon me' or 'upon me a Hajj walking.' If he said 'upon me is walking to the House of Allah' without mentioning Hajj or Umrah, one of the two rituals becomes obligatory by Istihsan. If he makes it Umrah, he walks until he shaves, unless he intended walking to the Mosque of Madinah, the Mosque of Jerusalem, or any mosque, in which case nothing is obligatory. His saying 'upon me is walking to Makkah or the Ka'bah' is like his saying 'to the House of Allah.' If he said 'upon me is walking to the Haram or the Sacred Mosque,' nothing is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa due to lack of custom in undertaking a ritual by that. The two said: the ritual is obligatory as a precaution. They all agreed that nothing is obligatory if he said 'to al-Safa, al-Marwah, Maqam Ibrahim, the curtains of the Ka'bah, its door, its waterspout, Arafat, Muzdalifah, the Prophet's Mosque, or mentioned a place of walking other than these, like saying 'upon me is going to the House of Allah' or 'departing.'
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It discusses the issue of a person who vows to perform Hajj walking. The author explains the virtue of walking based on a hadith that multiplies rewards, but notes that Abu Hanifa considered riding superior because walking might lead to disputes; however, the commentator reconciles that walking is more virtuous due to greater exertion, though riding is permitted to avoid hardship. The key dispute among later Hanafi scholars is where the obligation to walk begins: the relied-upon view is from one's home (customary meaning), while others say from the miqat or from the point of ihram. The commentator supports the home view with a narration from Abu Hanifa about a Baghdad resident. The obligation ends with Tawaf al-Ziyarah, not Tawaf al-Sadr. If one rides, compensation varies: a dam for most of the journey, charity for a small part. The hadith of Uqbah's sister is quoted to show that riding with a dam is allowed in case of inability. The passage then extends to vows of walking to the House without specifying Hajj or Umrah: it obligates one of the rituals by istihsan, and details specific wordings that are or are not binding. The view of Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is compared regarding 'walking to the Haram'.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform a specific act of worship, which becomes obligatory if the conditions are met.
مشي في الحج (mashy fi al-hajj): Walking as part of the Hajj journey, either as a vow or as a recommended act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the passage, from where does the obligation to walk begin for a person who vows to perform Hajj walking?
A) From the Miqat
B) From his home
C) From the point of Ihram
D) From the city of Makkah

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position: walking in a vowed Hajj is wajib, begins from one's home, ends with Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and riding without excuse incurs a penalty.

Vowed Hajj Discharged by Obligatory Hajj: Abu Hanifa vs Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on vowed Hajj vs obligatory Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a vowed Hajj is discharged by the obligatory Hajj according to Abu Hanifa and explain the disagreement with Muhammad, including the practical scenarios.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: the obligatory Hajj automatically fulfills a prior vow to perform Hajj.

This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a vow (nadhr) to perform Hajj. The core issue is whether performing the obligatory Hajj (Hijjat al-Islam) automatically fulfills a prior vow. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it does, while Imam Muhammad disagrees. Understanding this difference is crucial for determining the validity of a vow and the intention required when performing Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Dispute
Recognize that the ruling concerns a person who vowed to perform Hajj (nadhr) and later performs Hajj without specifying whether it is for the vow or for the obligatory Hajj.
The text contrasts two scenarios: one who has never performed Hajj and one who has already performed it.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person who has not yet performed the obligatory Hajj makes a vow to perform Hajj and then performs Hajj without specification, it counts as the obligatory Hajj and the vow is discharged.
The vow is directed to the act of Hajj itself, which is realized by the obligatory Hajj.
3
State Muhammad's Position
Imam Muhammad holds that the vow is a separate commitment and is not automatically fulfilled by the obligatory Hajj; a separate intention is required.
This is the intra-Hanafi disagreement.
4
Apply the Scenario for Those Who Have Already Performed Hajj
If a person has already performed Hajj, then vows to perform Hajj, and later performs Hajj, he must specify that it is for the vow; otherwise it becomes a supererogatory (nafl) Hajj.
This is agreed upon by both? Actually the text says 'as clarified in Fath al-Qadir', indicating the general Hanafi position.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: In a situation where a person vowing and then performing Hajj without specification, according to Abu Hanifa both obligations are fulfilled, while according to Muhammad the vow remains unfulfilled.
This affects whether one must repeat the Hajj to fulfill the vow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومقتضى الأصل أي القياس لا أصل الإمام محمد قوله : (يسقط بحجة الإسلام عند أبي حنيفة) الذي في الفتح عند أبي يوسف قوله : ليس له الرد بالعيب لأنه يمكنه إزالته بالتحليل ثم الحج المنذور يسقط بحجة الإسلام عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لمحمد، فإذا نذر الحج ولم يكن حج ثم حج وأطلق كان عن حجة الإسلام وسقط عنه ما التزمه بالنذر لأن نذره منصرف إليه، وإن كان قد حج ثم نذر ثم حج فلا بد من تعيين الحج عن النذر وإلا وقع تطوعاً كما حرره في فتح القدير. ومن نذر أن يحج في سنة كذا فحج قبلها جاز عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد، وقول أبي يوسف أقيس بما قدمناه في نذر الصوم.
His statement: (And the implication of the principle i.e., analogy, not the principle of Imam Muhammad. His statement: (It is discharged by the Hajj of Islam according to Abu Hanifa) which is in al-Fath according to Abu Yusuf. His statement: He does not have the option of defect because he can remove it by tahlil. Then the vowed Hajj is discharged by the Hajj of Islam according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to Muhammad. So if he vowed Hajj and had not performed Hajj, then he performed Hajj in an absolute manner, it counts as his obligatory Hajj and he is relieved of what he undertook by the vow, because his vow is directed to it. If he had already performed Hajj, then vowed, then performed Hajj, he must specify the Hajj as for the vow, otherwise it becomes a supererogatory Hajj, as clarified in Fath al-Qadir. Whoever vowed to perform Hajj in a certain year and performed Hajj before that year, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. Abu Yusuf's opinion is more in line with analogy, as we have previously discussed in the vow of fasting.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins by quoting a matn phrase about 'implication of principle' and then addresses the ruling that a vowed Hajj is discharged by the obligatory Hajj (Hijjat al-Islam) according to Abu Hanifa, but Muhammad disagrees. The commentator clarifies: if a person who has never performed Hajj vows to do so and subsequently performs Hajj without specifying, it counts as the obligatory Hajj and the vow is fulfilled; if he had already performed Hajj, he must specify that the later Hajj is for the vow, otherwise it is supererogatory. A related dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad concerns performing the vowed Hajj before the specified year: Abu Yusuf allows it, Muhammad does not. The commentator says Abu Yusuf's view is more consistent with analogy, referencing a similar issue in vows of fasting.

Key Terms
يسقط بحجة الإسلام (yasqutu bi-hijjat al-Islam): The vowed Hajj is cancelled/fulfilled by performing the obligatory Hajj (Hajj al-Islam).
مقتضى الأصل (muqtada al-asl): The implication of the original principle (often referring to qiyas or the default ruling).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Hajj counts as supererogatory and the vow remains
B) The Hajj counts as the obligatory Hajj and the vow is fulfilled
C) The Hajj is invalid because of the vow
D) The person must repeat both

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa: the obligatory Hajj automatically discharges a prior vow to perform Hajj, provided the person had never performed Hajj before the vow.

Vowed Hajj in a Specified Year: Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on performing vowed Hajj before the specified year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Abu Yusuf that performing a vowed Hajj before its specified year is valid, and contrast it with Muhammad's view that it is not.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf: performing Hajj before the vowed year is valid; Muhammad: it is not.

This passage presents another intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a vow to perform Hajj in a specific year. If the person performs Hajj before that year, does it fulfill the vow? Abu Yusuf says yes, citing analogy (qiyas) with a similar case in vows of fasting. Muhammad disagrees. Understanding this difference helps in advising those who make temporal vows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The scenario is a person who vows to perform Hajj in a specific year (e.g., next year) but performs the Hajj before that year arrives.
The dispute is about whether the early performance fulfills the vow.
2
State Abu Yusuf's Position
Abu Yusuf holds that performing Hajj before the specified year is valid and the vow is fulfilled.
His reasoning is based on qiyas with a similar ruling for fasting vows.
3
State Muhammad's Position
Imam Muhammad holds that the vow requires performance in the specified year, so early performance does not fulfill it.
The disagreement is on the strictness of the temporal condition.
4
Analyze the Analogy (Qiyas)
The text mentions that Abu Yusuf's view is 'more in line with analogy' and references a previous discussion on fasting vows.
This analogy likely treats the vow as a generic commitment to perform Hajj, not strictly bound to the year.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: If someone performs Hajj early, according to Abu Yusuf the vow is fulfilled; according to Muhammad the vow remains and must be performed again in the specified year.
The mufta bihi is not explicitly stated here, but Abu Yusuf's view is noted as more analogically sound.

Source Text

Buyer's Right to Release a Muhrimah
Ruling on buyer of a muhrimah: tahlil and intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a buyer of a slave woman in ihram, identify the valid methods of tahlil, and explain why the seller's tahlil is disliked while the buyer's is not.

Core Idea
Ownership of usufruct gives the buyer the right to release the slave from ihram, preferably without intercourse.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a nuanced scenario: a buyer purchases a female slave who is already in the state of ihram. What are the buyer's rights regarding her pilgrimage state? The ruling clarifies that the buyer can terminate her ihram (tahlil) without any sacrificial penalty, because the slave's usufruct belongs to him. However, the method and timing matter, and there is a distinction between the seller's and buyer's positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is buying a female slave who is in ihram. The ruling is that the buyer may release her (tahlil) and then have intercourse. Determine the hukm level: is it wajib, mubah, etc.?
The passage states she may be released without a sacrifice, indicating permissibility (mubah).
2
Understand the basis for the ruling
The reason given is that the slave's usufruct (manafi') belongs to the master (buyer). This gives him authority over her actions, including terminating ihram.
This is a fundamental Hanafi principle: ownership of usufruct grants control over the slave's religious obligations that compromise the owner's rights.
3
Distinguish between seller and buyer
The seller's tahlil of the slave is disliked (makruh) because the seller had given her permission to enter ihram. The buyer never gave such permission, so his tahlil is not disliked.
The key is consent: the seller's prior permission makes his revocation inconsistent, while the buyer's fresh authority faces no such contradiction.
4
Determine valid methods of tahlil
Tahlil is accomplished by an action, not by mere words like 'I release you.' Valid actions include cutting a nail, cutting hair, or intercourse. Intercourse also counts as tahlil.
The passage explicitly says 'tahlil does not occur by saying 'I release you' but by an action or by her action at his command (e.g., combing).'
5
Recognize the preferred method
Releasing by cutting nail/hair is better than by intercourse, because intercourse is the greatest violation of ihram and can even invalidate Hajj (cause corruption). The buyer should avoid it out of reverence.
This reflects a general fiqh principle: when an act is permissible but carries greater harm, the less harmful alternative is preferred (istihbab).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشتری محرمة حللها وجامعها لأن منافعها مستحقة للمولى فيجوز له تحليلها بغير هدي غير أن البائع يكره تحليله لا خلاف الوعد حيث وجد منه الإذن والمشتري لم يوجد منه الإذن فلا يكره تحليله قيد بكونها محرمة لأنها لو كانت منكوحة فليس للمشتري فسخ النكاح لأنه قائم مقام البائع وهو ليس له الفسخ بعد الإذن وأطلق في إحرامها فشمل ما إذا كان بإذن البائع أولا . وأشار بعطف الجماع على التحليل إلى أنه يحللها بغير الجماع كقص ظفر وشعر وهو أولى من التحليل بالجماع لأنه أعظم محظورات الإحرام حتى الفساد فلا يفعله تعظيماً لأمر الحج، ولا يقع التحليل بقوله حللتك» بل بفعله أو بفعلها بأمره كالامتشاط بأمره. وأشار إلى أن للمشتري أن يحلل العبد المحرم لما قدمناه، وإذا كان له منعهما وتحليلهما ليس له الرد بالعيب. وإلى أن الحرة لو أحرمت بحج نفل ثم تزوجت فللزوج أن يحللها عندنا بخلاف ما إذا أحرمت بالفرض فليس له أن يحللها إن كان لها محرم، فإن لم يكن لها فله منعها، فإن أحرمت فهي محصرة لحق الشرع فلذا إذا أراد الزوج تحليلها لا تتحلل إلا بالهدي بخلاف ما إذا أحرمت بنفل بلا إذن له أن يحللها ولا يتأخر تحليله إياها إلى ذبح الهدي كما قدمناه في باب الإحصار ولو أذن لامرأته في حج النفل فليس له أن يرجع فيه لملكها منافعها وكذا المكاتبة بخلاف الأمة. وفي فتح القدير : ولو جامع زوجته أو
And if he buys a woman in ihram, he may release her (from ihram) and have intercourse with her, because her usufruct belongs to the master; thus it is permissible for him to release her without a sacrifice, except that the seller's release of her is disliked because the seller had given permission, whereas the buyer has not given permission, so his release is not disliked. The condition is that she is in ihram, because if she were a married woman, the buyer cannot annul the marriage since he stands in the place of the seller, who cannot annul after permission. The statement is general regarding her ihram, covering whether it was with the seller's permission or not. He indicated by conjoining intercourse with tahlil that he may release her without intercourse, such as by cutting a nail or hair, and that is better than release by intercourse, because intercourse is the greatest violation of ihram, even causing corruption; so he should not do it out of reverence for Hajj. Tahlil does not occur by his saying 'I release you' but by his action or by her action at his command, such as combing at his command. He indicated that the buyer may release a male slave in ihram as we have mentioned. And if he has the right to prevent them and release them, he does not have the option of defect (in the sale). And also that if a free woman enters into a supererogatory Hajj and then marries, her husband may release her according to us, unlike if she entered obligatory Hajj; he may not release her if she has a mahram, but if she does not have one, he may prevent her. If she entered ihram, she is confined for the right of the Shari'ah; thus if her husband wants to release her, she is not released except with a sacrifice, unlike if she entered a supererogatory Hajj without his permission; he may release her and his release is not delayed until sacrificing, as we mentioned in the chapter of ihsar. And if he gave permission to his wife for a supererogatory Hajj, he cannot revoke it because she owns her usufruct, similarly for a mukatab slave, unlike an umm walad. In Fath al-Qadir: And if he has intercourse with his wife or...
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on scattered issues in the Book of Hajj. It explains the case of purchasing a slave woman who is in ihram. The buyer has the right to release her from ihram (tahlil) without offering a sacrifice, because the usufruct of a slave belongs to the master. The seller's release is disliked because he had previously allowed her to enter ihram, but the buyer did not; thus the buyer's release is not disliked. The buyer may use means other than intercourse, like cutting nails or hair, and this is preferable because intercourse is a major violation of ihram. Tahlil is not effective by merely saying 'I release you'; it requires an action. The passage also covers: the buyer's right to release a male slave; that the buyer cannot return the slave due to a defect if he can release them; and the case of a free woman who enters supererogatory Hajj and then marries—her husband can release her (unlike obligatory Hajj if she has a mahram). If she entered without permission, the husband can release her immediately without sacrificing. The passage ends with a reference to a ruling in Fath al-Qadir about a husband having intercourse with his wife.

Key Terms
محرمة (muhrimah): A female slave who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, with or without her master's permission.
تحليل (tahlil): Releasing someone from ihram, i.e., terminating the state of ihram by actions like cutting hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the seller had previously given her permission to enter ihram, whereas the buyer did not.
C) Because the buyer must offer a sacrifice, while the seller need not.
D) Because the seller is not allowed to perform tahlil at all.

Key Takeaway
A buyer of a slave in ihram owns her usufruct and can release her from ihram without sacrifice, preferably by actions other than intercourse.

Extended Rulings: Male Slave, Defect, and Free Woman
Additional rulings on tahlil: male slave, defect, free woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the buyer's rights regarding a male slave in ihram, explain why the buyer cannot return a defective slave if he can release them, and differentiate between rulings for a free woman in supererogatory vs. obligatory Hajj.

Core Idea
The buyer's right to tahlil extends to male slaves and blocks defect returns; a free woman's husband can release her from supererogatory Hajj, but not from obligatory Hajj if she has a mahram.

The passage continues with several important extensions: the same tahlil rule applies to male slaves; if the buyer has the power to release the slave, he cannot return her for a defect; and a free woman who enters supererogatory Hajj and then marries gives her husband the right to release her, subject to conditions. These rulings refine the broader principle of ownership and authority over pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for a male slave
The passage explicitly states that the buyer may also release a male slave in ihram. This confirms that the gender of the slave does not change the ruling.
The phrase 'وأشار إلى أن للمشتري أن يحلل العبد المحرم' clearly extends the rule.
2
Understand the impact on defect returns
If the buyer has the right to prevent the slave from performing Hajj or to release them, then he cannot return the slave for a defect after purchase. The reasoning is that the defect (e.g., the slave being in ihram) does not harm the buyer because he can remove that condition.
This is a specific application of the general principle that the option of defect (khiyar al-ayb) is negated when the buyer can rectify the defect.
3
Differentiate free woman cases
For a free woman who enters supererogatory Hajj (nafl) and then marries, the husband can release her from ihram. But if she entered obligatory Hajj (fard), the husband cannot release her if she has a mahram. If she has no mahram, he can prevent her from going.
The distinction hinges on the nature of the Hajj: nafl is more flexible, fard is binding unless exceptional.
4
Analyze the husband's authority with permission
If the husband gave permission for a supererogatory Hajj, he cannot revoke it because the wife owns her usufruct. Similarly for a mukatab (slave with contract of manumission), but not for an umm walad (slave mother of her master's child).
This reinforces the principle that ownership of usufruct (here the wife's) grants autonomy once permission is given.

The seller's release is disliked because he had previously allowed her to enter ihram, but the buyer did not; thus the buyer's release is not disliked. If she entered without permission, the husband can release her immediately without sacrificing. The passage ends with a reference to a ruling in Fath al-Qadir about a husband having intercourse with his wife.

حج النفل (hajj al-nafl): Supererogatory (voluntary) Hajj.

Vows of Walking: When Does a Promise to Walk Obligate Hajj or 'Umrah?
Explaining the obligation of walking when vowed and the effect of different phrasing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules to determine when a vow of walking to a sacred place obligates one of the two rites (Hajj or 'Umrah) and identify the role of custom ('urf) and precaution (ihtiyat) in the intra-Hanafi difference.

Core Idea
A vow to walk only obligates a rite if custom indicates commitment to it.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explores the nuances of vows (nathr) to walk to the House of Allah. It clarifies that not every mention of walking to a sacred place triggers an obligation. The ruling depends on custom ('urf) and intention, leading to a well-known intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn).

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the vow's exact wording
Determine what the person said: 'walking to the House of Allah', 'to the Haram', 'to Mecca', 'to the Ka'bah', etc. The precise phrase matters.
Phrases like 'to the House of Allah' customarily imply commitment to a rite.
2
2. Check if the wording belongs to the exception list
If the phrase refers to a specific location that is not customarily associated with Hajj or 'Umrah (e.g., Safa, Marwah, Maqam Ibrahim, Arafat, Muzdalifah, or any mosque), no obligation arises.
The exception also includes phrases like 'going to' or 'leaving'.
3
3. Apply the principle of istihsan for ambiguous vows
When the vow mentions walking to the House of Allah, the Ka'bah, or Mecca without specifying the rite, one of the two rites becomes obligatory by istihsan (juristic preference).
Istihsan here overrides qiyas in favor of custom.
4
4. Handle the intra-Hanafi dispute for 'Haram' and 'Sacred Mosque'
For vows to walk to 'al-Haram' or 'al-Masjid al-Haram', Abu Hanifa holds no obligation due to lack of custom. The Sahibayn hold that a rite is obligatory as a precaution (ihtiyatan).
This difference stems from differing weight given to custom vs. precaution.
5
5. Determine the practical ruling
If the vow matches the first category (customarily implying a rite), the person must perform one rite. If it falls in the exception or Abu Hanifa’s view on Haram, nothing is required. In fatwa, the mufta bihi is often the Sahibayn’s view (precaution), but this text does not specify.
Always consider the intention (niyyah) as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عجزها عن المشي بدليل الرواية الأخرى وأنها لا تطيق. وأطلق في الإيجاب فشمل ما إذا كان منجزاً أو معلقاً وما إذا قال الله على أو علي حجة ماشياً، ولو قال علي المشي إلى بيت الله الحرام ولم يذكر حجاً ولا عمرة لزمه أحد النسكين استحساناً، فإن جعله عمرة مشى حتى يحلق إلا إذا نوى به المشي إلى مسجد المدينة أو مسجد بيت المقدس أو مسجد من المساجد فإنه لا يلزمه شيء. وقوله على المشي إلى مكة أو الكعبة» كقوله «إلى بيت الله ولو قال علي المشي إلى الحرم أو المسجد الحرام فإنه لا شيء عليه عند أبي حنيفة لعدم العرف بالتزام النسك به. وقالا : يلزمه النسك احتياطاً. واتفقوا على أنه لا لزوم لو قال إلى الصفا أو المروة أو مقام إبراهيم أو إلى أستار الكعبة أو بأبها أو ميزابها أو عرفات أو المزدلفة أو مسجد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، أو ذكر مكان المشي غيره كقوله «علي الذهاب إلى بيت الله» أو «الخروج».
Its inability to walk is evidenced by the other narration, and that she cannot endure. And he was unqualified in making it obligatory, so it includes whether it is unconditional or conditional, and whether he said 'upon me is Allah' or 'upon me is a Hajj walking'. And if he said 'upon me is walking to the Sacred House of Allah' and did not mention Hajj or 'Umrah, one of the two rites becomes obligatory by istihsan. If he makes it an 'Umrah, he walks until he shaves, except if he intended by it walking to the Mosque of Medina or the Mosque of Jerusalem or any mosque, then nothing is obligatory upon him. And his saying 'upon me is walking to Mecca or the Ka'bah' is like his saying 'to the House of Allah'. And if he said 'upon me is walking to the Haram or the Sacred Mosque', then nothing is upon him according to Abu Hanifah due to lack of custom of committing to the rite by it. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the rite is obligatory upon him as a precaution. Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal consequences of a vow (nathr) to walk to the House of Allah. It begins by noting that if the person is unable to walk, a narration indicates she may not be obliged. Then it explains that the vow to walk, when unqualified, includes unconditional and conditional forms. If someone says 'upon me is walking to the House of Allah' without mentioning Hajj or 'Umrah, one of the two becomes obligatory by istihsan. However, if the intention is to walk to another mosque, no obligation arises. There is a difference of opinion on phrases like 'walking to the Haram' or 'the Sacred Mosque': Abu Hanifa says nothing is required due to lack of custom ('urf), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the rite is obligatory as a precaution (ihtiyatan). They unanimously agree that specific locations like Safa, Marwah, etc., do not create an obligation. The key principle is that the vow of walking only becomes binding if it is customarily understood as a commitment to Hajj or 'Umrah.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to derive the obligation of one of the two rites when the vow is ambiguous.
عرف ('urf): Custom – the basis for Abu Hanifa's ruling that there is no obligation for certain phrases.
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precaution – the method used by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad to obligate the rite.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Nothing is required.
B) One of the two rites is required.
C) Only 'Umrah is required.
D) Only Hajj is required.

Key Takeaway
A vow of walking creates an obligation only when the wording customarily implies a commitment to Hajj or 'Umrah; otherwise, the general rule is no obligation, with an intra-Hanafi difference for certain sacred phrases.

Fulfilling a Vowed Hajj: Timing and Specification
Explaining that a vowed Hajj is fulfilled by the obligatory Hajj, and the rule for vows to a specific year.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on fulfilling a vowed Hajj with the obligatory Hajj and on early performance, and explain the key differences between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
A vowed Hajj can be fulfilled by the obligatory Hajj, and early performance is valid by analogy to fasting vows.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses two contested issues within the Hanafi school regarding vows (nathr) of Hajj. The first issue is whether a vowed Hajj is automatically discharged by performing the obligatory Hajj (Hijjat al-Islam). The second concerns performing a vowed Hajj before its specified year. Both issues reveal the use of qiyas (analogical reasoning) and the principle of specification (ta'yin). Understanding these disputes sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi legal reasoning to similar vow-related cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage presents two distinct legal questions: (1) Does the obligatory Hajj fulfill a previously made vow to perform Hajj? (2) If one vows Hajj in a specific year, is it valid to perform it earlier?
These are independent issues, each requiring separate analysis.
2
Analyze Issue 1: Abu Hanifa vs. Muhammad
Abu Hanifa holds that if a person who has never performed Hajj vows Hajj and then performs Hajj without specifying, the performed Hajj counts for both the obligation and the vow. Muhammad disagrees, requiring a separate Hajj for the vow. Their difference stems from whether the vow is 'valid for' (munsarih ilayh) the obligatory Hajj.
The key term is 'munsarih ilayh' (understood to refer to).
3
Analyze Issue 2: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
If someone vows to perform Hajj in a specific year, Abu Yusuf permits performing it before that year, drawing an analogy (qiyas) with a vowed fast that can be performed early. Muhammad insists on adhering to the specified time.
Abu Yusuf's opinion is described as 'aqyas' (more analogical).
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
For Issue 1: If the person has already performed obligatory Hajj before vowing, the vowed Hajj must be specifically intended; otherwise it becomes nafl. For Issue 2: If one performs early, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf but not according to Muhammad. The mufta bihi is not explicitly stated, but the text favors Abu Yusuf's qiyas.
The practical ruling differs depending on which opinion is followed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الحج المنذور يسقط بحجة الإسلام عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لمحمد، فإذا نذر الحج ولم يكن حج ثم حج وأطلق كان عن حجة الإسلام وسقط عنه ما التزمه بالنذر لأن نذره منصرف إليه، وإن كان قد حج ثم نذر ثم حج فلا بد من تعيين الحج عن النذر وإلا وقع تطوعاً كما حرره في فتح القدير. ومن نذر أن يحج في سنة كذا فحج قبلها جاز عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد، وقول أبي يوسف أقيس بما قدمناه في نذر الصوم.

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues regarding vows of Hajj. First, if a person who has never performed the obligatory Hajj (Hajj al-Islam) vows to perform Hajj and then performs Hajj without specifying, Abu Hanifa holds that the performed Hajj fulfills both the obligatory Hajj and the vow. Muhammad disagrees, requiring a separate performance for the vow. If the person has already performed Hajj al-Islam, the vowed Hajj must be specifically intended; otherwise, it becomes a supererogatory Hajj. Second, if someone vows to perform Hajj in a specific year but performs it before that year, Abu Yusuf considers it valid, drawing an analogy with a vow of fasting that can be performed early. Muhammad requires adherence to the specified time.

Key Terms
نذر (nathr): A vow to perform an act of worship, making it binding.
حجة الإسلام (hijjat al-Islam): The obligatory Hajj, which is one of the pillars of Islam.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning, used by Abu Yusuf to permit early performance.
منصرف (munsarih): Valid for or applicable to; used to describe that the vow is understood to refer to the obligatory Hajj.

Key Takeaway
A vowed Hajj can be fulfilled by the obligatory Hajj (Abu Hanifa), and it is valid to perform it early (Abu Yusuf), but specification is needed if the obligatory Hajj was already performed.

Buying a Slave in Ihram: Rights of Dissolution and Zufar's Dissent
Commentary on buyer's right to dissolve slave's ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on dissolving the ihram of a purchased slave, explain the method of tahlil, and identify the practical consequence of Zufar's opposing view.

Core Idea
Ownership of usufruct gives the buyer the right to dissolve the slave's ihram without a sacrifice.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rule when a person buys a slave woman who is already in ihram. The buyer may dissolve her ihram and even have intercourse, because he owns her usufructs. The commentator clarifies the method of tahlil, contrasts the case of a free wife, and includes a minority view from Zufar that the buyer cannot dissolve, allowing a return for defect. Understanding this ruling clarifies the intersection of sale and pilgrimage prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Name the act: buying a slave woman in ihram. What is the ruling? The buyer may dissolve her ihram and have intercourse.
This is a permissive ruling (jawaz) based on ownership.
2
Trace the legal basis (ta'lil)
Why may he dissolve? Because her usufructs belong to the master. The buyer stands in the seller's place, and the seller originally had the right to dissolve.
The key term: manafi' (usufructs) are owned by the master.
3
Distinguish the method of tahlil
How is tahlil performed? By actions like cutting nails/hair, not just by words. Intercourse is also a tahlil but is discouraged because it is the greatest violation of ihram.
Tahlil is not a verbal formula but a physical act that removes ihram.
4
Extend to related cases
The passage extends to: free wife who enters nafl ihram without husband's permission (husband may dissolve), vs. obligatory ihram (husband may not if she has a mahram). Also, a husband cannot revoke permission for nafl hajj.
The underlying principle: who owns the usufructs controls the ihram.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Zufar disagrees: the buyer does not have the right to dissolve. Therefore, he may return the slave for a defect because she remains in ihram, harming utility.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if Zufar's view is followed, the buyer has the option of return (khiyar al-ayb).

Source Text

تعلق به
قوله: (ولو اشتری محرمة حللها وجامعها) لأن منافعها مستحقة للمولى فيجوز له تحليلها بغير هدي غير أن البائع يكره تحليله لا خلاف الوعد حيث وجد منه الإذن والمشتري لم يوجد منه الإذن فلا يكره تحليله قيد بكونها محرمة لأنها لو كانت منكوحة فليس للمشتري فسخ النكاح لأنه قائم مقام البائع وهو ليس له الفسخ بعد الإذن وأطلق في إحرامها فشمل ما إذا كان بإذن البائع أولا . وأشار بعطف الجماع على التحليل إلى أنه يحللها بغير الجماع كقص ظفر وشعر وهو أولى من التحليل بالجماع لأنه أعظم محظورات الإحرام حتى الفساد فلا يفعله تعظيماً لأمر الحج، ولا يقع التحليل بقوله حللتك» بل بفعله أو بفعلها بأمره كالامتشاط بأمره. وأشار إلى أن للمشتري أن يحلل العبد المحرم لما قدمناه، وإذا كان له منعهما وتحليلهما ليس له الرد بالعيب. وإلى أن الحرة لو أحرمت بحج نفل ثم تزوجت فللزوج أن يحللها عندنا بخلاف ما إذا أحرمت بالفرض فليس له أن يحللها إن كان لها محرم، فإن لم يكن لها فله منعها، فإن أحرمت فهي محصرة لحق الشرع فلذا إذا أراد الزوج تحليلها لا تتحلل إلا بالهدي بخلاف ما إذا أحرمت بنفل بلا إذن له أن يحللها ولا يتأخر تحليله إياها إلى ذبح الهدي كما قدمناه في باب الإحصار ولو أذن لامرأته في حج النفل فليس له أن يرجع فيه لملكها منافعها وكذا المكاتبة بخلاف الأمة. وفي فتح القدير : ولو جامع زوجته أو أمته المحرمة ولا يعلم بإحرامها لم يكن تحليلاً وفسد حجها، وإن علمه كان تحليلاً. ولو حللها ثم بدا له أن يأذن لها فأذن لها فأحرمت بالحج ولو بعد ما جامعها من عامها ذلك لم يكن عليها عمرة ولا نية القضاء ولو أذن لها بعد مضي السنة كان عليها عمرة مع الحج، ولو حللها فأحرمت فحللها فأحرمت هكذا مراراً ثم حجت من عامها أجزأها عن كل التحللات بتلك الحجة الواحدة ولم لم تحج إلا من قابل كان عليها لكل تحليل عمرة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم .
وفيه خلاف زفر قال : ليس له ذلك فله الرد بالعيب كما في الفتح والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب.
Related to it: His saying: (And if he buys a woman in ihram, he may dissolve her ihram and have intercourse with her) because her usufructs are owned by the master, so it is permissible for him to dissolve her ihram without a sacrificial animal, except that the seller dislikes his dissolution, without disagreement regarding the promise, since permission came from him (the seller) and the buyer did not have permission from him, so his dissolution is not disliked. It is restricted to her being in ihram because if she were a married woman (mankuha), the buyer could not annul the marriage because he stands in the place of the seller, and the seller does not have (the right of) annulment after permission. And it is unqualified in her ihram, so it includes whether it was with the seller's permission or not. And he indicated by conjoining intercourse to dissolution that he may dissolve her (ihram) without intercourse, like cutting a nail or hair, and that is better than dissolution through intercourse because it (intercourse) is the greatest of the prohibitions of ihram, even corruption, so he should not do it out of reverence for the affairs of Hajj. And dissolution does not occur by his saying 'I have dissolved you', but rather by his action or by her action at his command, like combing hair at his command. And he indicated that the buyer may dissolve the ihram of the male slave in ihram, as we have previously mentioned, and if he has the right to prevent them and dissolve their ihram, he does not have the right to return (the slave) due to a defect. And also that if a free woman entered ihram for a supererogatory Hajj and then married, her husband may dissolve her ihram according to us, contrary to if she entered ihram for an obligatory Hajj; he may not dissolve it if she has a mahram; if she does not have one, he may prevent her (from entering ihram), and if she entered ihram, she is muhsara (blocked) for the right of the Shari'a, so when the husband wants to dissolve her ihram, she does not become halal except with a sacrificial animal. Contrary to if she entered ihram for a supererogatory (pilgrimage) without permission; he has the right to dissolve her ihram, and his dissolution of her is not delayed until the slaughter of the sacrificial animal, as we have mentioned in the chapter on ihsar. And if he gives permission to his wife for a supererogatory Hajj, he may not revoke it because she owns her usufructs, and likewise the mukataba (slave contracted for emancipation), unlike the female slave. And in Fath al-Qadir: If he has intercourse with his wife or his female slave who is in ihram and he does not know of her ihram, it is not a dissolution (tahlil) and her Hajj is invalidated; if he knows, it is a dissolution. And if he dissolves her ihram, then it occurs to him to give her permission, so he gives her permission and she enters ihram for Hajj, even if after he had intercourse with her in that same year, there is no 'umrah upon her nor intention of making up (qada'). And if he gives her permission after the year has passed, there is upon her an 'umrah with Hajj. And if he dissolves her ihram, and she enters ihram, then he dissolves her again, and she enters ihram repeatedly in this manner, then she performs Hajj in that same year, that one Hajj suffices for all the dissolutions; but if she does not perform Hajj except the next year, there is upon her an 'umrah for each dissolution. And Allah the Almighty knows best. And in this matter there is a disagreement from Zufar: he said that he (the buyer) does not have that (right to dissolve), so he has the right to return (the slave) due to a defect, as stated in Fath. And Allah the Almighty knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and the final destination.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rule: 'If someone buys a slave woman in ihram, he may dissolve her ihram and have intercourse with her.' The commentator explains that the buyer may do so because he owns her usufructs, without the need for a sacrificial animal. Unlike the seller, who may have disliked the dissolution, the buyer's action is not disliked because he did not give permission. The rule is restricted to a slave in ihram; if she were a married free woman purchased, the buyer could not annul the marriage. The buyer can dissolve her ihram by actions like cutting hair or nails, which is better than intercourse. Dissolution is not valid by mere words. The commentary extends to free women: a husband may dissolve his wife's nafl ihram if he did not permit it; for obligatory ihram with a mahram, he cannot; without a mahram, he can prevent her entry. For nafl without permission, immediate dissolution without sacrifice is allowed. A husband cannot revoke permission for a supererogatory Hajj because she owns her usufructs. Cases from Fath al-Qadir are cited regarding intercourse with a wife or slave in ihram: if he knows, it constitutes tahlil; if unaware, it invalidates her Hajj. Repeated dissolutions and ihrams: if she performs Hajj the same year, one Hajj suffices; otherwise, an 'umrah is required for each dissolution. Finally, Zufar disagreed, holding that the buyer does not have the right to dissolve, so he may return the slave for a defect.

Key Terms
محرِمة (muhrima): A woman in the state of ihram for Hajj or 'Umrah.
تحليل (tahlil): The act of releasing someone from ihram, making permissible what was prohibited.
زفر (Zufar): Abu Hafs Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a prominent Hanafi jurist with independent views.
منافع (manafi'): Usufructs; the benefits and services derived from a thing or person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the consequence if a buyer purchases a slave woman in ihram and then dissolves her ihram?
A) The buyer must offer a sacrificial animal.
B) The buyer cannot return the slave due to a defect.
C) The slave's Hajj is automatically invalid.
D) The seller must approve the dissolution.

Key Takeaway
The buyer of a slave in ihram may dissolve her ihram without sacrifice, based on ownership of usufruct; Zufar's opposing view would allow the buyer to return the slave for defect.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
