Rulings on a Slave Woman's Ihram and the Owner's Authorization
Series of rulings about a slave woman in ihram and her owner's tahlil actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which an owner's tahlil of his slave woman is valid and apply the rulings regarding subsequent ihram and compensation.

Core Idea
An owner's tahlil is valid only if he knows of her ihram; ignorance invalidates her hajj.

This passage from the Book of Hajj addresses a specific scenario involving a slave woman who enters ihram. The owner's authority over her extends to the ability to cause her to exit ihram (tahlil), but that power is conditional on his knowledge. The text explores various sequences of tahlil and re-ihram, and concludes with a difference from Imam Zufar regarding the owner's right.

Guided Path
1
Determine the owner's knowledge
Identify whether the owner knew of the slave woman's ihram at the time of tahlil. This is the key condition for validity.
2
Identify the consequence of tahlil with/without knowledge
If the owner knew, the tahlil is valid and her hajj is valid. If he did not know, the tahlil is invalid and her hajj is invalid.
3
Handle the scenario of re-permission after tahlil
If the owner later permits her to re-enter ihram for hajj, the timing matters: if within the same year, no compensation; if after the year, she must perform umrah with hajj.
4
Handle repeated tahlil and subsequent hajj
If the owner repeatedly performs tahlil and she re-enters ihram, then performs hajj in the same year, one hajj suffices. If hajj is performed the following year, each tahlil requires a separate umrah.
5
Note the scholarly difference with Zufar
Zufar holds that the owner has no right to perform tahlil, so it constitutes a defect in the slave woman, giving the buyer the option to return her.
The relied-upon position is the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج/ مسائل منثورة ١٣٥
أمته المحرمة ولا يعلم بإحرامها لم يكن تحليلاً وفسد حجها، وإن علمه كان تحليلاً. ولو حللها ثم بدا له أن يأذن لها فأذن لها فأحرمت بالحج ولو بعد ما جامعها من عامها ذلك لم يكن عليها عمرة ولا نية القضاء ولو أذن لها بعد مضي السنة كان عليها عمرة مع الحج، ولو حللها فأحرمت فحللها فأحرمت هكذا مراراً ثم حجت من عامها أجزأها عن كل التحللات بتلك الحجة الواحدة ولم لم تحج إلا من قابل كان عليها لكل تحليل عمرة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم . وفيه خلاف زفر قال : ليس له ذلك فله الرد بالعيب كما في الفتح والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب.
His slave woman who is in ihram, and he does not know of her ihram, his tahlil was not valid and her hajj is invalid. If he knows, then it is valid. If he performed tahlil for her then it occurred to him to permit her, so he permitted her and she entered ihram for hajj, even if after he had intercourse with her in that same year, she does not have to perform umrah nor intend qada. If he permitted her after the year had passed, then she must perform umrah along with hajj. If he performed tahlil for her and she entered ihram, then he performed tahlil and she entered ihram repeatedly, then she performed hajj in that same year, that one hajj suffices for all the tahlils. If she did not perform hajj except the following year, then she must perform an umrah for each tahlil. And Allah knows best. And there is a difference of opinion from Zufar: he said he does not have that right; so the buyer has the option of defect due to the defect, as in al-Fath. And Allah knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and refuge.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Hajj presents a series of rulings regarding a slave woman (ummah) who is in a state of ihram. The owner's act of making her exit ihram (tahlil) is only valid if he is aware of her ihram; if unaware, her hajj becomes invalid. Different scenarios are detailed: if the owner later permits her to re-enter ihram for hajj, even after intercourse, she does not need to compensate with umrah or qada. However, if the permission comes after the year, she must perform umrah with hajj. If the owner repeatedly performs tahlil and she re-enters ihram, then if she performs hajj that same year, it suffices for all tahlils; otherwise, each tahlil requires a separate umrah. The passage concludes with a disagreement with Zufar, who holds that the owner does not have the right to such tahlil, and thus the buyer of such a slave woman can exercise the option of defect (khiyar al-ayb) because the tahlil is considered a defect. The relied-upon position is the one given in the main text, and the reference to al-Fath indicates the preferred view.

Key Terms
تخليل (tahlil): The owner's act of making his slave woman exit the state of ihram, usually by commanding her to do so.
أمة محرمة (ummah muhrimah): A slave woman who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slave woman is in ihram and her owner makes her perform tahlil without knowing she was in ihram, what is the ruling?
A) The tahlil is valid and her hajj is valid.
B) The tahlil is invalid and her hajj is invalid.
C) She must perform an additional umrah to compensate.
D) The owner must seek her permission.

Key Takeaway
The validity of an owner's tahlil hinges on his knowledge of the slave woman's ihram; ignorance invalidates both the tahlil and her hajj.
